<Author>mlsmn
<Content>Lovely hotel, convenient location in Venice We enjoyed staying for 2 nights at the Antiche Figure in Venice last month. Upon arriving we were offered to move to suites (we had 2 rooms booked) at the 'annex' location down the small street next to the hotel. The rooms were well decorated with many amenities. The suites did appear to be quite a bit larger than the double and triple rooms we were shown in the main hotel. The suites did not have views of the Canal, but that was not a priority for us as we spent most of our time exploring the lovely city of Venice.The location of the hotel is very convenient for arrival and departure from Venice. We were able to walk from the Piazzale Roma after arriving by air, then leave Venice via the train station directly across the canal. The bridge across the canal is somewhat difficult with large luggage to reach the train station. Venice is easy to walk in, we walked to and from St. Mark's square, although the water bus was also available.The staff at the hotel was very friendly and helpful. They were kind to give us restaurant recommendations and show us the nearest church to attend Christmas Eve services. The breakfast room was large, the buffet was nice with meats, cheese, eggs, fresh fruit and a large variety of breads and cereals each day. We would be pleased to stay at this hotel if we are able to return to Venice in the future.

<Author>Francesca_Vincenti
<Content>Best Value For Money Small but perfect in many ways.Nothing beats a 3-Star Hotel with a 5-Star service and accommodation offer! The staff ensure constant personalised  friendly assistance. Your stay here is guaranteed to be comfortable, pleasant and hassle free. Conveniently located within a 5 minute walk from the central bus terminus at Piazzale Roma (the final stop for all vehicles before Venice) and situated directly opposite (across the Grand Canal) the Train Station, you are perfectly set within reach of all major attractions. The Vaporetto (public water bus service) from close to the Train Station here is only éˆ§?.50 to Piazza San Marco.The hotel staff will surprise you with their unsurpassed knowledge of current events in the city, cultural or historical exhibtions and more. The rooms are incredibly decorated in the style reminiscent of pure Venetian romance. They are kept constantly preened and spotless by their 'attention to detail' housekeepers. I loved walking in to find a Baci chocolate on my pillow every night and I would let it slowly melt in my mouth while I smiled like the princess I imagined myself to be while gazing out of my window onto the Canale Grande.The breakfast was always fresh with a wide choice of healthy food items to choose from or for those who want to indulge  spoil themselves during their stay, there is always a delectable spread of tarts, fresh crossants and other mouth-watering goodies!I highly recommend the place. It's the best value for money anyone can get around venice....and believe me, the staff's genuine friendly attitude is priceless. I am definitely returning for a personal vacation with my partner and shall mark this hotel as my top choice!Francesca VincentiMalta

<Author>LauraSSpringfield_IL
<Content>Loved the hotel, loved the service--fantastic location! We stayed in Venice right before the most recent flooding . . .the location from the main bus terminal Piazelle Roma made it really convenient and CHEAP to get to and from the airport on the airport buses. When you land and go to the main baggage area, look for a little window (Information) off to one end of the airport and you can buy the bus passes for the airport bus and waterbuses for however many days you'll be using it. The water buses were very short walk from the hotel, as people have mentioned, --even a gondelier station right outside the hotel door! Pay attention to the directions from the buses, because you want to go over the little green metal bridge (about 40 steps) to walk to the hotel. You'll come right to it then.I booked after looking at the hotel website and checking everything out on Trip Advisor---which was so helpful for planning our trip there and to Vienna. The front desk was very good about emailing all info and confirmations. I even wrote a few days before since I booked the room months in advance; they always replied promptly etc. They genuinely wanted us to have a good stay.The front desk staff was very accommodating---gave us names of places to try for eating, gave us an early morning cappucino and continental breakfast at 5:00a.m. the day we left for an early flight. They offered us a room upgrade for a nominal amount, which was really worth it to be facing the Grand Canale. We were there when it was cold, so the tourists were not there enmasse, loud etc. It was great room . .. great coffeemaker in the room fully stocked with teas and coffee, and fantastic amenities like shampoos, toothbrushes with paste etc. So nice since it's such a pain with the airline restrictions now. Flat screen TV. The hotel has recently been remodeled; it's clean and lots of marble in the bathrooms, nice decor. Even the inside room we looked at was nice, but a good deal cozier (small) than the one we ended up with. Either way, they have nice rooms.The staff couldn't have been kinder and more helpful! (They will make you a nice cappucino in the bar and bring it to the breakfast area if you ask, and then will just charge it to your room. It's lovely, better than the coffee machine, which isn't terrible either) The bar also has some little sweet treats to buy and maybe even some sandwiches; I didn't check. No full restaurant service tho, but a cute little nook in the lobby across from the bar, if you want to enjoy something downstairs, which people did I noticed. The breakfast I thought was very good---quite a big spread of all kinds of baked items, boiled eggs, fruit, cereals, yogurt and so forth. A lovely big breakfast room--enough to handle all the clientele. The staff weren't pushy, either, about getting you out of the breakfast, which was nice since you're on vacation! They arranged the FREE water taxi to Murano (you can take a water bus home) which was really nice, although the taxi takes you to a small, artist gallery glass factory which is pretty pricey--the cheapest thing we saw was 60 Euro, but we did enjoy the little demonstration and looking in the showroom. NO obligation to buy; the hotel staff even mentioned that, but you do have to steel yourself for the sales pitch. The last demonstrations were around 3 or 4:00 in the afternoon, so watch the timing. It's a short walk from there up the hill to the main street and canal where there are plenty of other shops and restaurants. You catch the water bus from there.One thing to watch in the restaurants--especially near San Marks Square. There are two menu prices in many---one for take away items, drinks etc. and another price for sitting down, which can make it considerably more expensive. We were there without the big crowds, which was sooo nice. We enjoyed touring the Basilica and the Doges' Palace--esp. the prisons (very foreboding), but we enjoyed wandering around the streets just as much! Got a lot in because there was no waiting time, but it was chilly and probably felt even colder because you're on the water, so we were glad we had heavy coats and cashmere! Our stay was definitely enhanced because of the Hotel Antiche Figure; I'm so glad we found it online. We did book early and I'd advise that because I'm sure it fills up fast because of the price and the good reviews. We would love to find another hotel like this one if we visit another romantic spot in Italy again. sometime.  
<Date>Dec 13, 2008

<Author>mwhitmoe
<Content>Glorious Hotel What a glorious hotel!! My new wife and I had been to Italy on our honeymoon. We had just come from Milan where we had a disappointing hotel stay (I booked without consulting Trip Advisor). Furthermore, I had heard rooms (and particularly bathrooms) in Venice were tiny. So my expectations were lowered.When we arrived at the Venice train station, we took a short walk over a nearby bridge and viola, the hotel was just a few doors down right on the Grand Canal. Francesca greated us with warmth and ebulience (noting that it was our honeymoon). The lobby/bar area was charming and cozy. She personally escorted us to our room (312). It was beautiful and surpringly spacious. The was a desk, a separate sitting area with a table and two chairs. The bathroom was also spacious and nicely appointed with murano (sp?) style glass fixtures. Everything was also spotless! The bed was large and comfortable. There was a tasteful work of art, and the room had a very elegant, gilded element to it. But the best part was the windows. Another reviewer noted that he did not think a deluxe view room was worth the extra money unless it was on the second floor, which have small balconies. While I would agree balconies are even better, I would respectfully disagree. We had a nearly panoramic view of the activities all along the upper part of the Grand Canal. It is true that the hotel does face the main train station, and the bus station is visable. But it was easy for me to let my eyes wander down at the canal level, I loved the sights and sounds of the waterway. However, once we clossed the windows we were pleased to discover the soundproofingwas quite satisfactory; we slept well at night, It was a deluxe room, and came with a supply of complimentary coffee and teas. Internet is free of charge in the rooms. When we mentioned that we had a laptop, but no connecting cable, she had one brought up for us to use. There was a nice coninental brekfast every morning that I would recommend for 7 Euros. Since anywhere in Venice is theoretically no more than about a 30 minute walk, or a comparable vaparotto (water bus) ride, its location works quite well. The front desk, whether it be Francesca or the very helpful and humorous man whose name I cannot recall that splits time with her, is alway there to help with a restaurant recommendation or a suggestion about what to do.Overall a complete treat to stay there!

<Author>SabreSailor
<Content>A Perfect Stay at the Perfect Hotel We booked the Antiche Figure as a result of the reviews in TripAdvisor, and we were not disappointed! We were in Venice for a few days before leaving on a cruise on the Zuiderdam.We arrived on September 27 after flying from NY through Madrid, taking the 3 Euro blue bus from the airport to Piazzale Roma (the only place in Venice that vehicles are allowed). The hotel is about a 10 minute walk from Piazzale Roma (it would have been five minutes as they suggest, but we were each pulling two large wheeled suitcases up and over the two bridges which were a bit challenging).When we arrived at the hotel we were greeted by the manager, who offered us a choice of two rooms - and insisted that we go up and choose. The rooms are beautiful (even though we had one the lower cost red rooms) and the bath was marble with a wonderful shower.Once up and the room chosen, our bags arrived in about two minutes. We then went down (it was 2:30pm) and asked the manager if there was anywhere in the area to grab a quick lunch. He directed us down an alley next to the hotel to a series of small shops including a bakery and pizzeria.Having eaten, we returned and asked if there was a short walk we could take before we started thinking about dinner. He pulled out a map, told us how to get Vaporetto (water bus) tickets (a 3-day pass), and mapped out a route for us to San Marcos via water and then a walk back. It seemed aggeressive, but it was perfect! By the way, you can pretty much throw your map away in Venice. Despite what you read, you are never really lost. You see yellow signs everywhere for San Marcos, Rialto, Piazzala Roma, and Ferrovia (train station). Since the Antiche Figure is near both the train station and Piazzala Roma, just follow the signs until you get to the Grand Canal!The staff sent us to Osteria al Veccio Pozzo for dinner, a simple restaurant where we got the simple light meal we needed before crashing.The next morning, we went to the Antiche Figure's breakfast room where we found just about anything you'd want - from delightful pastries to cereal to juice, to meats and cheeses, boiled eggs, etc. The hostess was consistent with the rest of the staff - going overboard to be helpful - everyone was even asked whether they wanted cappuccino!Back for more advice from the staff, and then a day's run around the city. Their recommendation for dinner was Trattoria Antica Bessetta, where we eventually resorted to a map - it's not easy to find! But was it worth the effort! We met the owner, who told us about a trip that morning to the Venice Pescheria (open air fish market near the Rialto) where he found the perfect turbot, which we ordered. He brought it to the table in the foil in which is was baked, and then worked like an artist to prepare the perfect presentation on our plates. This place is well worth a visit, but make reservations. It was fully booked when we left....Another restful night at the Antiche Figure, followed by check out and detailed directions on how to find the free shuttle bus that runs between the Piazzale Roma and the pier (we had previously contacted Holland America Line and they told us that there was no such bus) which was right where the staff told us it would be.Visiting the Antiche Figure is like going home, even though it may be your first visit. The staff makes you feel like family, and they have practiced their art well. We spoke to others who had stayed at other hotels - even one in famous Bauer for more than twice the money - and none could rave about the hotel, its staff and service, as we could.If you're going to Venice, do yourself a favor. Stay at the Antiche Figure - you won't be disappointed!  
<Date>Oct 14, 2008

<Author>ScreenName021
<Content>Lovely place, great location Really lovely little hotel opposite the station on the Grand Canal. Our room didn't really have a view (an alley way) but it was clean, extremely comfortable and very Venetian - marble and murano glass. We checked in very late due to flight problems so maybe if we'd been there earlier in the day we might have had more of a view. But can't complain. It was a really nice room. And it sounds like a odd thing to commend a hotel on, but the air conditioning was great - quiet and efficient. A night's sleep in a what would otherwise be a good hotel is so often ruined by the whirring and whining of bad air con. And good double glazing too - Venice is a noisy place. We slept so well there. Well done to the maintenance staff. The staff are what made the stay. All of them are very friendly and helpful. Breakfast is continental buffet and plenty of choice. You can have breakfast in the dining room or outside the hotel by the canal. And a night cap from the bar sitting at the tables outside the hotel watching the vaporettos and gondolas go by is an extremely pleasant way to end the day. The hotel is very handy for transport too. We really enjoyed our stay there and will definitely go back next time we're in Venice.

<Author>TigluvsItaly
<Content>Wonderful experience I stayed here 9/13-16 with 2 girlfriends. We reserved 2 rooms. When we arrived on a cold, rainy day, we found that they had only one room for us and had not seen the 2nd request for a room. However, they accomodated us by giving us a large triple room with a view of the Grande Canal. The staff was right up there to set up the room. The next day, they gave my friend her room one floor up and they let me and my other friend stay in the triple for a great price (remember the room had an awesome view!) They were very apologetic about the whole mistake. The managers were very helpful and if you called down to request help ie) with bags, they would be up in 60 seconds flat. No joke!! The breakfast was adequate. The room and bathroom was spacious and beautifully decorated. I liked standing on the small balcony and watching boat traffic on the canal. It was a little far from San Marco but there is a vaporetto nearby. I preferred walking so this wasn't a big deal to me. It is right across the canal from the train station. On a side note, ladies, some of the male staff here are VERY easy on the eyes ; ) Overall, the experience here at this hotel and the city in general was wonderful!

<Author>Brude
<Content>Brilliant hotel, great location, fantastic staff This is a lovely smaller hotel situated in a great location. Access from Marco Polo Airport is around 3 euro per person by direct bus to Piazzale Roma just a few hundred metres away while the hotel itself is directly opposite the train station. Position is on the Grand Canal with most of the sites a pleasant walk away or of course a water boat ride. Lots of restaurants in the area so you have a great choice but of course Venice is not somewhere you come for the variety and quality of its cuisine, pizza is its staple dish. On arrival at the hotel we were welcomed by the most pleasant and enthusiastic staff I have ever encountered. We were offered an update to their newly opened suites for surcharge but no pressure to take the deal. We visited our pre booked room which was lovely but the suites were really special and suited our needs better so we took the offer. The suites have a lounge with kitchen area, double bedroom and top quality bathroom, well worth the extra. Our time in Venice was terrific, Venice is a lovely quiet and safe city due to the total lack of motor vehicles, you really discover what we have lost when you can walk around smelling the air not fumes, hearing the sounds of peoples not Lorries and can turn a corner without fear of being flattened. Breakfast at the hotel was a good quality continental and again the staff were wonderful, full of smiles and welcomes. This is a wonderfully convenient hotel which is maintained in excellent condition and is staffed by highly trained and pleasant people, what more could you want?

<Author>Alphaville1976
<Content>our stay at Antiche Figure was excellent ... My wife and I spent our honeymoon in Italy recently: 5 nights in Rome, 3 in Florence, and 2 in Venice. I heard about Antiche Figure through the reviews here on TripAdvisor, and I decided to book a room for two nights based on a combination of the positive reviews and it's location on the Grand Canal.Just a few comments about it's location: it is a 20 minute walk or so from St. Mark's Square, so this is something for people to consider. I actually like this aspect of the hotel ... my wife and discovered so many interesting streets on our way to the main square. One of the streets was somewhat hidden from the main tourist areas (we found it after visiting Murano), but it contained one of the best restaurants we've ever been to (ex. my wife's dish was squid braised in ink). So, if you really want to discover Venice by walking, I would highly recommend this hotel due to it's location. Another thing to consider is that you can reach this hotel via the local boat system (which is akin to say, Rome's bus system). In fact, it was really fun to visit San Georgio (an island near main Venice) and then take the boat back to our hotel. In the process, we saw some of the other neighboring islands and it really is a nice boat ride. For these reasons, I consider the location to be a plus.Now, for the actual hotel: our room was very nice. It was very clean with a great view of the canal. All of the accomodations were great: comfortable bed, nice bathroom with spacious tub and US-compatible electrical outlet. We didn't get the most expensive room, but I would say that it was a very nice room and definitely very romantic if you are considering this aspect for your trip. We did have the breakfast, and we both felt that this was the best of any of the hotels we visited in Italy. There was a wide assortment of different cereals, coffee products, pastries, meats, and cheeses. A definite plus!Lastly, I would say that the staff was very polite and helpful. We didn't ask too many questions because we like to explore and find things ourselves. Nonetheless, they were always very helpful and willing to suggest things when asked. Overall, a great experence. A very nice hotel with a great location: nice, romantic rooms; great breakfast; and friendly staff.

<Author>Neanne
<Content>I'd go back in a flash A nice little hotel tucked into a busy area of Venice, the Antiche Figure is directly across the Grand Canal from the train station. To get there from the station, simply gross the bridge, turn to the right and itéˆ¥æªš about the equivalent of a city block at most. The bus station to the airport is a short walk beyond the hotel and across a couple of bridges and you can travel to either Marco Polo or Treviso for very little money. With the trains, gondolas, heavy foot traffic and constant coming and going of the vaporetti, you might at first wince at the prospect of a room fronting the canal, however, we spent two nights there and slept like babies.Rooms are smallish but comfortable, with a worn-around-the edges sort of elegance with plenty of closet space, in room safe and fridge, TV, phone, antiqued furniture and silk drapes, and the spacious and elegant baths which seemed to be the standard during our stay in Italy. Personnel is crisply efficient and consistently available. There is an elevator, an ample Continental breakfast of fruits, yogurt, cereal, and pastries or croissants. There is a machine for American coffee and staff will quickly offer you freshly made cappuccino if they spot you in front of the apparatus. Granted the Antiche Figure is a long walk to Piazza San Marco (which can be obviated by traveling via vaporetto) and perhaps itéˆ¥æªš not the most glamorous spot in Venice, but the view is still lovely. Frankly, after the hordes of tourists in Piazza San Marco, I found the area rather an oasis.

<Author>Garysbogie
<Content>Great hotel  We stayed at the Hotel Antiche Figure just prior to embarking on a cruise from Venice. The hotel is quaint and beautifully maintained. Our room overlooked the Grand Canal. The only detraction was the smaller windows. We were on the top floor and it appears those below have larger windows and hence, a better view. Regardless, we were thoroughly satisfied with the room. The bed was soft, the bathroom exquisite! They furnish robes, slippers, the whole nine yards! A nice buffet breakfast is furnished. A small bar off the lobby provides alcoholic libations as well as cappucinos and cafe Americano. The location is convenient, being right across the canal from the train station and a short walk from the bus terminal. Water taxis are available at the train station and private taxis are also available. It's about a half hour walk to St. Mark's, but it's pleasant with numerous shops to browse around in or small cafes to grab a cappucino. There are a lot of cafes nearby, so going hungry won't be a problem. Overall, I couldn't give a higher recommendation to a hotel. Beware that everything in Venice has to be offloaded and transferred to a boat before delivery, so extra expenses are involved. With the dollar not holding up to the Euro, everything in Venice is expensive. Regardless, it's a city you shouldn't miss and the Hotel Antiche Figure will make it even more rewarding. Ciao!

<Author>Fredbear
<Content>Wonderful Hotel We stayed at this hotel for two nights to celebrate my birthday, and couldn't have asked for better.We had booked one of the red rooms, but on arrival were informed that one of the suites was available in an adjacent building down a short Calle. We were offered it at a reduced rate of an additional éˆ§?0 a night instead of the usual éˆ§?0 with breakfast included. Once we had seen the picture, we were hooked and when we saw it, we knew we had made the right choice. It was lovely, and looked very recently done. There was a king size fourposter bed,draped in white muslin. Dressing table, and wardrobe all beautifully decorated. The walls are covered in cream striped fabric, and there are very beautiful wall lights and table lamps. The windows were dressed with acres more white muslin and luxuriously draped curtains. The room was equipped with a security box in the wardrobe and a very efficient mini bar, not to mention the wall mounted flat screen TV.The bathroom was spotlessly clean, and equipped with a superb shower cubicle. Everything from spare toothbrushes, razors , shower caps, shoe polishing sponges and a very handy sewing kit. Huge, white fluffy bath sheets too.The airconditioning unit was very efficient. The double glazing kept out all noise, and the shutters were excellent too. It was hard to believe that you were only a couple of hundred yards away from the Grand Canal, you heard nothing, not even the church bells!The entry hall was all marble, as were the two flights of stairs you had to climb to get to our suite. Entry was via a buzzer system operated from the reception area, then a security card key to your suite. We were never kept waiting to get in form more than a minute.The hotel has tables and chairs right on the Grand Canal, and a shady area to the side under two large sun shades. We sat there for a couple of hours every afternoon with a drink or two just watching Venice pass by. Entertainment was provided by the Gondoliers based at the Gondola station right outside the notel, their banter is wonderful to watch. Breakfast was very good, cheese and cold meats, boiled eggs yoghurts, cereals, juice and a wide array of pastries and fresh fruit. We got down later one morning, nearer 10 than 7, and there was still plenty to choose from. Fresh coffee is made for you from an impressive machine at reception. A choice of teas was also available.The breakfast room was very well presented, and you can also breakfast outside or in the bar area. We did all three during our stay.The reception staff and all the waiting/bar staff were extremely helpful and friendly. Nothing was too much trouble.Reception was full of flowers, and an enduring memory of the hotel will be the scent of lilies, gorgeous!We will definately be returning, and recommending it to anyone we know is intending to visit Venice. Almost forgot, it is even easier to find it when you arrive at Piazza Roma than the website says, and takes less than 10 minutes to walk even with a case. They were also more than happy to store our luggage before and after check out, which was brilliantEverything is right there on the doorstep. You cannot go wrong.We were asked when we left if we could think of anyway the stay could have been better, we honestyly couldn't hink of anything at all. On reflection, a chest of drawers might be a useful addition to Room 515, but in the scale of things, how minor is that?Pretty much faultless, we loved it.

<Author>Ryans5
<Content>Wonderful hotel! We used TripAdvisor with some trepidation to help us find a good hotel for our two night stay in Venice prior to a cruise. We were thrilled beyond words to find that everything we had read about the Antiche Figure hotel in this forum was accurate. The rooms (we traveled with another couple) were very nice, one was larger than the other, but the smaller one was still very functional. The decor was lovely, bathrooms especially. The rooms were very quiet, as well. The breakfast was quite good and could be eaten in either the breakfast room or outside right by the canal. The staff was extremely friendly and helpful. Definitely trust their restaurant recommendations, they were excellent. The hotel is a short walk (ten minutes max) from the Piazzelle Roma but it does require going over two bridges to get there, so pack accordingly! The hotel staff were able to direct us exactly to where the free bus was in Piazzelle Roma to take us to the cruise port. I would not hesitate to recommend this hotel to everyone, it has a wonderful charm about it and it's location, away from the busier parts of Venice and near the major port, make it ideal for cruisers.

<Author>Thombtc
<Content>Fantastic Location My husband and I just returned from a Mediterranean cruise and stayed at Antiche Figure for 2 nights before the departure of the Emerald Princess from Venice. Once flying into Venice we took the ACTO bus to Piazza Roma. The bus is right outside the exit of the baggage area of the airport so it was very convenient. Look for a yellow ticket machine. Once you put your 3 euros in ( it gives change), validate it in another machine near it before the bus comes. When you arrive at Piazza Roma (very busy area) you have a decision to make before going to the hotel. How will you get there. We are in our 60's and pulling our luggage over 2 stepped bridges nearly killed us. If you are young, you could walk to the hotel. If not,. take a water taxi at the Piazza. ( Even young people were struggling with their luggage) The hotel was fantastic and the room 411 overlooking the canal was so much fun. When you take a shower, you can open the bathroom window and look at the beautiful green dome right next to you. There are two windows that you can open over the canal and see and hear all of the action, but once you close the windows, we couldn't hear anything. Amazing! We could see the Railway Station right across the canal. The breakfast in the morning was typical European and we loved the little cappicino machine. Take your breakfast out to the tables in front of or the side of the hotel to eat. Don't miss the action. We couldn't understand why people would eat in the breakfast room. The staff was outstanding and very pleasant. They answered any question you could think of and drew maps for anywhere. We can't say enough about the hotel and you won't be disappointed. My husband and I have traveled to Europe 5 times and would definitely stay at this hotel again. We paid about 300 euros a night for the room ( directly booked, but don't forget, you are on the canal and nothing is cheap in Venice). Going to the cruise ship, we shared a taxi with another couple we met a the hotel and then it was cheaper. Ask the desk if someone would need to also go to the ship. We paid 40 euros instead of 80 and it was well worth it. It is farther than you think to the cruise terminal if you have 2 suitcases a piece and dragging them over many steps on bridges. Have fun!  
<Date>Jul 13, 2008

<Author>travel JR
<Content>Great small hotel away from the madness Wonderful small hotel right on the Grand Hotel. Located away from the madness of the tousit areas...yet diretly across the canal from the train station and a few blocks walk to the bus station...the 2 ways into and out of Venice. The front desk people are great...reallyu care about their guests...and very helpful in finding neighborhood restaurants. One of the great bargains of Italy is the 24-hour pass on the water buses...take your own tour of Venice by day and night and go see the islands (Burano and Murano). Tip: BUy the ticket in early evening, go for a tour that evening..and then use it for the next day to see the islands. We found food in Vencie to be expensive and not great...but try to find the true neighborhood restaurants for an interesting evening and good food.We were careful regarding pickpockets but did have any problems.

<Author>DCM.Dart
<Content>A Great Hotel - go there! We stayed at this hotel in June 2008 and all the rave reviews were right on! The hotel is beautiful and the staff are all uniformly pleasant and go out of their way to be helpful and welcoming. This location is excellent because it's away from the main tourist areas of San Marco Square but is located near water bus stops and you can get anywhere you want easily and quickly.Only 1 warning - This is not a hotel for people who are frail, with bad backs or with disabilities. If you arrive from the airport by bus, this hotel requires you to traverse 2 bridges from the Piazzale Roma each with at least 10 steps up and back down. Or if you arrive at the train station which is literally across the canal from the hotel, you must climb a bridge with 50 steps up and the same number down...easy with no luggage but quite a workout if you are carrying 50 lb. bags with you. Be forewarned.Make sure you get restaurant recommendations from the front desk staff. All were very good and we were never disappointed. All in all, an excellent hotel experience and I would unhesitatingly recommend it to any traveller.

<Author>DownUnderPerth
<Content>What a find! We are 2 seniors from Australia who just spent 4 weeks travelling by train through southern Germany, Austria, Slovenia and northern Italy. All of our accommodation was booked online, but our 3 night stay at Hotel Antiche Figure was the best. First of all the hotel was easy to find since it is located directly across the Grand Canal from the main train station. Upon arrival we were warmly greeted and told our room was ready, but a newly-renovated suite nearby was offered for the same price. We opted for the beautifully decorated suite with a living area, kitchenette, large bedroom with canopy bed and complete bathroom with all mod-cons. Breakfast was served each morning in the main hotel. The manager and his staff spoke perfect English. Nearby restaurants, patronized by the locals, were recommended. Advice on the ferries and sightseeing hints were given. Even a water taxi ride and guided tour through one of the glass factories on Murano Island were arranged for us with 15 minutes notice. We could not have wished for a more pleasant stay.

<Author>jayhawkinden
<Content>Just as good as everyone says! We booked a double deluxe canal view room for 2 nights for the beginning of our honeymoon. Our check in was smooth and the front desk personnel were wonderful.LOCATION: Superb! We came into Venice by train and the hotel is located directly across the canal from the train station. The most difficult portion is dragging two 50 lb luggage bag over the bridge. There are only steps, no smooth part to pull them! The other benefit of this location is that is located next to a vaperetto stop (water bus) that takes you wherever you want to go. If you desire to walk (which we did), it takes only about 20 minutes to walk to St. Marks Square and about 10 minutes to Rialto Bridge. Frankly you have so much fun walking you don't even notice the length!ROOM: Our room was very spacious for a European room. Beds were firm as to be expected, but fine. The view is really nice, but a little noisy in the morning with all of the water traffic. I really didn't care. The bathroom was great with a deep tub, double sinks, robes, and tons of hot water!FOOD: We didn't eat at the hotel. We ate in the town.SERVICE: The front desk personnel are amazing! They wil help you find anything, explain how to get there in detail, and put it on a map. All of this will a pleasant, friendly attitude!I didn't post any pictures, because mine are all the same as everyone else's.

All of the staff (I apologize I do not know all of their names) were wonderful. Each guest is treated like a valued customer. The lovely lady at the front desk was so pleasant when I arrived. She took the time to explain all of the main sites and options for accessing Venice. Linda (the very nice lady in the breakfast room) makes you a great cappuccino in the morning and is very pleasant. It is a nice way to start your day. The breakfast selection was great (meats, cheeses, cereals, pastries and juice). The location - it is right across the canal from the train station. You exit the train station to the left, cross the bridge and turn right and you are at the hotel. You do not have to drag your luggage on boats and canals. It is very convenient. In addition, the vaporetto stop (Ferrovia) is across the canal so you can easily access all of the sites. Tip:you can buy a 48 hour ACTV pass for 26.00 Euros or a 72 hour pass for 31 Euros. Walking is also possible with the signs that point you to San Marco and Rialto. I recommend a walk at night in particular. The room - I was upgraded to a beautiful suite which was located beside the hotel. It was spotlessly clean with excellent housekeeping service. The bed was very comfortable and the bathroom was large with a shower/tub combination. The suite had a full kitchen and two TVs. The toiletries were very nice and replaced daily.The hotel also has a very nice bar and at night you can sit at your table and enjoy a glass of wine while overlooking the canal. TIP: I enjoyed a lovely meal at Trattoria al Ponte Tel: [-] Address: Ponte del Megio (Calle Larga), Santa Croce 1666 The sea bass was excellent!I cannot wait to return to Venice and to this hotel. Thanks again to all of the staff at the Hotel Antiche Figure for your hospitality.

<Author>BostonNolefan
<Content>It's Really As Good As All of the Reviews Say It Is! My wife and I visited Venice from May 8-12 and we spent two nights at the Hotel Antiche Figure before boarding our cruise ship. We read these reviews before booking the room and trust me (a complete stranger) staying there was one of the BEST decisions that we ever made. The hotel is on the northern portion of the grand canal adjacent to the Scalzi bridge. We hadn't been to Venice before, so we didn't know what this location meant. It's within a very short walk from the bus stop from the airport (Piazza le Roma) and across from both the train station and a vaporetto stop. This means that you can actually take the bus from the airport (~3 Euros/person), be dropped off at Piazza le Roma, and reasonably walk to the hotel with a small suitcase. (In full disclosure you still have to cross two bridges, though).We're young and found no problem making the walk. We can't imagine having to lug our suitcases around to the hotels further down the canal. Our room was on the top floor (deluxe blue decor, check out the website) overlooking the canal. It was really beautiful and they have an elevator which made the trip up easy. The room was very nice. Nice furniture, well lit, spotless, and it appeared newly renovated (not sure if it was, or if it has just been well taken care of). It was larger than the hotels we stayed at elsewhere in Europe. The bathroom was top notch, large, beautiful with marble and Murano glass fixtures It also had two sinks.Everyone at the front desk was friendly and helped us navigate through this beautiful city. They spoke excellent English (we started to feel guilty because we don't speak Italian) and took great care to make sure that we were happy with our stay. I wish we could have stayed longer, but alas the boat had to set sail. That brings up another point. While the cruise ship port is relatively close, it is too far to trek on foot. You can either take a water taxi (they are literally parked directly in front of the building, or you can walk to Piazza le Roma and take a bus provided by the port authority (our bus was free). Less than 5 minutes drive to the cruise terminal.Breakfast consisted of breakfast meats, cheeses, coffees, and breads. It was very good.We made use of the free computer in the lobby with internet access. I think that there is wifi access in the rooms (but don't quote me on that). We were pressed for space so we didn't pack a computer. We will definitely be staying here again when we return to Venice. The cleanliness, size of the room, the view, the location, breakfast and staff made it special. If you choose to stay here you'll be happy with your decision!  
<Date>May 26, 2008

<Author>mginabq
<Content>Excellent experience - worth the price We stayed two nights at the Hotel Antiche Figure in Venice, April 28 and 29, 2008. I selected this property based on the TripAdvisor reviews because the trip to Italy was a surprise for my husband's 60th birthday, and I wanted things to be as close to perfect as they could be. I made the right choice, so many thanks to all of you who stayed there before us and wrote reviews.The hotel sits on the Grand Canal immediately across from the train station, which is very convenient. We lucked out as we were crossing the bridge and a young many offered to carry all our bags for 10 euros. It was a bargain! (Note: If you're coming from Piazzale Roma, there is a porter service via boat that will take you and your luggage for 35 euro - also a great bargain given the number of bridges you have to cross.)I splurged on the deluxe canal view room and was glad I did. While it is true that straight across you see the train station, that is definitely outweighed by the opportunity to watch the passing traffic in the Canal. The rooms are generously-sized, exactly as pictured on the hotel's website, immaculately clean, AND the bathrooms are huge, particularly by European standards.Every staff member with whom we interacted was professional, pleasant and helpful both before we arrived, by making restaurant recommendations and reservations, and after we got there, by answering our numerous questions and arranging a water taxi to get us to the airport when we departed. Francesa and Michele were lovely and tried to anticipate our needs.There is a computer for guests' use in the lobby, or if you travel with your own notebook, as we did, you can request a network cable at the desk to use in your room.The breakfast was excellent. We laughed when an American family came into the breakfast room, inspected the food, turned up their noses and promptly announced there was nothing to eat. I don't know what they expected because both days there were hard-boiled eggs, several kinds of meat and cheese, three types of cereal, abundant pastries, croissants and breads, juices and freshly-made cappuccinos and espressos.Both evenings we were there, we sat out in the little cafe area they have facing the Canal and had grappa while we watched the passersby.All in all, it was a lovely ending to our three-week trip. We will certainly return to Venice - it's a fabulous city where walking everywhere is safe and doable - and when we do, we will stay at the Hotel Antiche Figure.One last note: if you're going to Italy, learn some Italian. I did, and it was most rewarding to see how appreciative the people were. No one ever laughed at the numerous errors I'm sure I made and instead I heard again and again, Brava!

<Author>jdawg
<Content>Wonderful Antiche Figure My husband and I stayed at Hotel Antiche Figure last week of March for our first visit to Venice. The hotel is perfectly situated right by the water near the airport shuttle depot and the Ferrovia (train station). This is a big factor if you plan to take the train to other parts of Italy and have a luggage or two, or if you will take the train to Venice. Hotel is across from sestiere of Cannaregio, which has a lot of gelato places and restaurants.We upgraded to a deluxe room for 30 euros a night including breakfast. Not bad at all. The room was nicely decorated and the bathroom quite roomy. We had 3 windows that overlooked the water and the street. Our room was on the second floor and contrary to what most people said they experienced at hotels in Venice and Italy as a whole, it was quiet at night and even early morning. We kind of expected it would be noisy, but we're surprised in a very good way that it wasn't. Traditional Italian breakfast had quite a bit of options and cappuccino was better made by one of the servers than from the machine. All in all, I would highly recommend this hotel to everyone. It's romantic yet not cheesy. The concierge was very helpful and nice, too. I'd stay here again if I come back to Venice. Another one I highly recommend is the church of Santa Maria Gloriosa dei Frari. The exterior looks rather plain but once you set foot in, you'll be more than amazed. Jaw-dropping, really. They said it rivals St. Mark's Basilica for top billing and I completely agree. Don't miss it.

<Author>Londonlover7977
<Content>Loved It!! This was my second stay at the Antiche Figure. This first time we stayed in a red room (superior) which was fairly big with a good size bathroom, beautifully decorated, and if we stuck our head out of the window had a view of the canal. This last time I was there I was offered to upgrade for 20EUR more to the blue room (deluxe). I decided to go for it as we were only there for 1 night. Just gorgeous with a tiny balcony overlooking the Grand Canal. Large room and bathroom with double sinks. As others have said, it's directly across from Santa Lucia train station. You do have to cross a tall bridge so hopefully you packed lightly. To get to the bus stop to go the airport it's a few minutes walk away crossing 2 or 3 small bridges.It does take about 30 minutes to get to San Marco but you can take a vaporetto (the stop is in front of the train station) which takes about 25 minutes with the stops if you're tired of walking.The staff is wonderful. Free internet access in your room if you have a laptop and computer you can use in the lobby if you don't. In the lobby my daughter used her ITouch but could not access the internet from our room.I will definitely stay here again next time I go to Venice.

<Author>nalindap
<Content>Brilliant Excellent little place and keeps the costs down. This was a lovely little hotel that we staying in for 5 nights. It is situated accross from the train station and a short walk from the bus drop off aswell. It has water taxi drop off's right outside. There was no noise from the train station. We got into the airport and got blue bus into the main bus drop off and then walked for 10 mins to the hotel. The service and welcome was excellent. They offered to upgrade us but we declined to try and keep to the budget we had set. The room was nice and clean. We had one of the red rooms which had no view but they dress the windows up to make it look better. The views from the blue rooms would be over the canal and would be very nice. We got a 3 day travel pass which I highly recommend as it allows you to travel on the water taxis as much as you want. You are not really walking distance to the main site so taking the water taxis is a must. To be fair its really nice to travel up and down the canal and take in the sights. The hotel doesn't have a restaurant but there are plenty of places to eat accross the bridge ( only a short 5 min walk) and the taxis run till late from the middle of town. The hotel staff were very good at telling us the best places to see in the short time we had. They also had their own water taxi that would take you to the nearby islands at a time of your choosing.Throughly recommend the hotel if you are looking for a budget trip and a hotel that is pleasant.

<Author>snarkyarchy
<Content>All the charm of Venice After reading extensive reviews of hotels in Venice, I chose this hotel for our two night stay in March 2008. We had requested a room for three people and I was a bit apprehensive of what we were going to get, but could not have been more pleased with the room we were given.Upon check in, the staff was very friendly and gave us a briefing of where we were in relationship to all the major attractions. We were offered an upgrade for a suite in an adjacent building for a few more Euro, but opted to keep the room we booked. It was a beautiful room that fit a queen size bed and roll-in twin comfortably with a very large bathroom that looked like it was recently renovated. It was done in beautiful stone tiling with ample counter space, glass sconces, a shower, and bidet. If you stuck your head out the bathroom window, you could actually see the Grand Canal. The room itself was very clean and decorated accordingly with the old world charm of Venice.To some, the location may seem far from places like the Rialto (a 10-15 minute walk) or Piazza San Marco (a 20 minute vaporetto ride), but it proved extremely convenient to the train station (from where we arrived) and to Piazzale Roma where all the taxis and shuttles depart from to the airport (from where we left.) The only word of warning is that you will need to carry your luggage over the Scalzi Bridge (around 80 steps) from the train station) and two other bridges if you're heading to Piazzale Roma. It's a small price to pay for the great location and sure beats rolling your luggage to a hotel around Piazza San Marco or lugging it onto a water taxi.The area felt very safe and easy to find your way back after wandering all the streets and canals (just keep following the signs that say Ferrovia). Getting lost is the quintessential experience in Venice and it's how you discover some amazing architecture, shops, and restaurants.We had breakfast at the hotel on our last day and enjoyed the simple buffet of pastries, fruit and coffee. The free internet terminal in the lobby was also a nice bonus. I would definitely recommend this hotel to anyone willing to stay a little bit away from the major sites, but appreciates great service, charming rooms, and is in need of some good cardio getting those bags over the bridges.

<Author>SFBayMommy
<Content>Found nothing wrong here Am always interested in how hotels get such high rankings on tripadvisor. After staying here, i think the answer is: you walk away with nothing to complain about and you realize how rare that is. This hotel was great - not the best hotel of course - but for the price, it's great. I guess it is the absence of bad reviews that puts this hotel in such a high position. There wasn't any one thing that was great - but everything was above average. And if you're spending your own money, you won't feel like you overspent here. This hotel charges you for nothing extra (the internet wi-fi for free was a big plus) except late-afternoon beverages or drinks and mini-bar items. It's refreshing to walk away from a hotel and not have a bunch of extra charges on your bill.I've read all the reviews and everyone seems to be in agreement - staff is fabulous, location is excellent. The only things I'd add: yes, the floors/ceilings are thin. Hearing the water running (loudly) through the walls/ceiling was surprisingly loud. Not worth a bad review, but worth a mention. And yes, beds are extra firm - could have asked for another room probably, but wasn't worth the energy. Also, on the plus side: there's a laundromat right behind the hotel and right near the residences (where we stayed). It's great to have access to a washer/dryer even if you don't think you'll use it. And when you check out, they actually ask you if you have suggestions for them - and sound like they really want to know, which is great! Arrivaderci

<Author>Fred_Carno
<Content>A little Gem Stayed at this hotel last week for 3 nights, booked mainly on TA reveiws but also on price. Hotel is very easy to find from bus station, and easy to access with luggage. <Author>annabinnie
<Content>Lovely room, even lovelier service I booked at the Antiche Figure on the basis of Tripadvisor reviews, and I'm so glad we did. The Location is great, as the others say, near to the train station and perfect for the water ferries all around. We also upgraded to one of their suites - a junior suite, which is not in the hotel itself but down the adjoining street, tucked away in a very very quiet spot - I slept like a log every night. The suite was a little small, but very bright, with a lovely comfortable four-poster and a massage shower, and for a three night stay, a perfectly adequate size (especially somewhere like Venice, and especially for the price). The best thing though was the service: after arriving very tetchy and frazzled after the airline losing our luggage, we received the warmest welcome I can remember having in any hotel, and given a cup of coffee while the receptionist took the lost luggage report and said We'll take care of that for you, and went off to ring them on my behalf. They kept an eye on the situation and phoned me as soon as the bag arrived (they did - not, say, the airline, who were supposed to) and sounded as happy as I did that it was there.The breakfast is simple but fine, the room (that we stayed in, at least) really quiet and lovely, the location excellent - far enough away to make a difference in terms of price, but easy to reach everything. I can't recommend this hotel highly enough. I've been back 9 hours and already told three friends they should book there...

<Author>mycaseispacked
<Content>Lovely hotel The hotel is in an excellent location fronting the Grand Canal and a short walk from the rail station and coach station. We arrived by bus from the airport - the number 5 from outside the arrival hall straight into the city bus station - The hotel was a 5 minute walk from the bus station. You only need to cross two bridges and then its pavements all the way to the hotel door. We stayed for one night at the end of our trip around the Veneto area.The reception staff were excellent - warm, welcoming and spoke excellent english. We were on a room only basis and decided not to have breakfast at the hotel (at a small additional cost) so cannot comment on the quality of the food.The room was large, well decorated and clean. We had a room on the first floor with windows to the side alley which meant it was quiet. We had a disabled equipped room so no bath but the bathroom was like a wet room with a walk in shower. Shower was nice and hot and plenty of towels. The lack of bath did not bother us. The bed was large and comfortable and we had a great nights sleep. The only minor thing that stops me giving the hotel an excellent rating is that we had a glass light fitting which clinked and rattled when ever the person in the room above walked around. This got a little annoying but not enough to ruin our stay. It might just be me being slightly intollerant and the person upstairs being a tad heavy footed!?There is a mini-bar in the room but no tea of coffee making facilities. On returning to the hotel late and cold at night we fancied a coffee and the bar man kindly made a silver tray up of tea and coffee for us to take up to our room. The cost was very reasonable (about 6 euro) given the cost of a coffee when out in the city during the day!Location wise, you exit from the front door and a bridge crossing the grand canal is just to the right. On the opposite side of the Canal is a vaporetti stop for most routes. We had a 36 hour ticket which covered us for unlimited travel on the bus from the airport to the city, access on all the vaporetti - even out to Murano and the Lido - and back to the airport. You can also follow the signs through the city on foot to San Marco, the Rialto etc... which are a nice walk away.Overall, we were very impressed with the hotel - its location, staff, decor and cleanliness and would certainly stay here again when we return.  
<Date>Feb 29, 2008

<Author>Mark_S_Leeds
<Content>Great hotel, perfect location We stayed in this lovely hotel for 4 nights, staff were very helpful and friendly. The room was exceptionally clean and well fitted, if not particularly large, and the bathroom had a bath and an excellent shower. The location is great, a short walk from both the Piazzale Roma (where all the buses stop) and the Ponte di Cannaregio (where the airport water bus stops), right opposite the Scalzi bridge to the train station and close to loads of good local restaurants and cafes in Santa Croce, San Polo and Cannaregio (in particular we liked Osteria 40 Ladroni in Cannaregio, which is a fantastic seafood restaurant with more locals than tourists, but still very friendly).St. Mark's Square is only a 30-40 minute walk away (or a Vaporetto ride for 6 Euros) but the walk is so picturesque it's well worth doing.If I was to stay in Venice again I'd definitely stay here...

<Content>Friendliest hotel in Venice, A Must! Well, what a fantastic hotel. The friendliest place I have ever stayed. Went there Feb08 to confess my undying love for my man, and the hotel staff made sure our stay (and the moment) was perfect. Arranged the gondola and champagne at rock bottom prices. <Author>shazt
<Content>Great location, hotel  Very nice suprise! The rooms and bathrooms were very clean and tastefully decorated and a decent size (even had a bidet), not at all the older tired look we expected. We took a public bus from the airport to the last stop - Pizzale Roma and from there it was a ten minute walk over two bridges - a little odd with all the suitcases but you see lots of people doing it (no ramps on the bridges so you have to deal with the stairs) - very cheap commute about 3GBP, unlike I believe a water shuttle. Very conveniently located, close to many stores and restaurants and a walk to St. Marks Square. The hotel will even arrange a complimentary water shuttle to the glass factory (no sales pressure watch the glass blowing and leave if you like). We had breakfast each morning sitting outside by the canal which was lovely (self serve continental breakfast was adequate). Opposite the hotel is a beautiful church (interior is very impressive - take the 2 mins to check it out). Outside the hotel you can even get a gondala. We were allowed to drink our own wine bottles in the seating area by the canal (instead of their bar service). Staff were wonderful and very helpful! Would not hesitate to stay again.

<Author>KaB24
<Content>Well worth its 3 star+ rating My husband and I stayed at this hotel 6th-9th January 2008. I booked this hotel as a birthday surprise for my husband and although we had stayed in Venice before and loved the hotel we chose then, I decided on the Antiche Figure as the reviews were excellent and it was so central. We were not disappointed, it was an easy walk from the Bus station, over 2 small bridges. The welcome we received on arrival was very friendly and throughout our stay our every need was catered for even down to a chocolate on our pillows, reception staff organized the secret itinerary tour of Doges Palace (16 euros) which was fascinating, they also organized a free taxi transfer from the hotel's landing stage to a Murano glass factory  showroom which I would not recommend as although they say there is no obligation to buy we definitely felt uncomfortable not buying any of the beautiful glassware on display, also there was no route through to the rest of the island which meant we had a wait of 30 mins before we were picked up and dumped at Fondamente Nuove the nearest vaporetto stop on Venice. We later returned to Murano by vaporetto (No 42) and enjoyed walking through and seeing the rest of the island. We enjoyed our stay and would definitely use this Hotel again.

<Author>PeterandChristel
<Content>Perfect Location and Perfect Service I took my partner there for his birthday...and so what a birthday he had. We arrived about 21h00 on the Wednesday evening so I phoned just to let them know that we were still coming but just a little late so they wished us a great trip and not to worry about anything. When we arrived, the receptionist Eddi (not sure about the spelling, sorry) showed us a restaurant to go and grab a quick bite and told us about few things to do in the area, She was really nice and smiley...which is always nice.Our room was lovely and cosy ( the red one) with a great Chandelier in the room and Bathroom (I think probably from Murano Glass Factory) we even had a view over the grand canal...bonus... but still very quiet during the night.. In the morning breakfast was between 7-8h00 and 10h00 so you could have a little lying in bed...nice.The walk from the Piazzale Roma was really a 5 minutes walk tops...I was really worried to get lost but it is very easy to find the hotel, they have lovely christmas light on the front of the hotel so you can not miss it. Just look at the comments below someone gave great directions to get to the hotel.As long as you have a map of the island you really can't get lost .After a couple of days you really get the hang of it and it is pretty easy to find you way around. From the hotel to San Marco Square you are talking about a 20 minutes walk through the lovely street full of christmas lights and lovely little boutiques. Venice is a trully remarquable place, full of history and beautifull architecture, December is a great month to go as well as you get some very good deals on Gondola Ride, Place to Visit (Murano Glass Factory was free to visit....(to be honest it was a really quick visit with a quick demonstration of the blowing glass technique but very interesting).The only negative things I will have to say unfortunately is prepare yourself to fing some grumpy Italians in some places like restaurants ( oh another thing don't go for the Menu Touristico, it is much better to order from the main menu)or museem, we were very lucky because all the staff from the hotel made us feel very welcome and they were always really smiley and happy to help but it will not be the same everywhere.Anyway it was a very great romantic break for me and my husband to be...so can not wait to come back and of course stay again at the Antiche Figure...

<Author>scooterguy
<Content>Venice's Best Kept Secret! The Antiche Figure delivers what it promises and more! The plain exterior of this hotel belies what is really inside. We stayed here for 3 nights following a 14-day cruise. We were amongst several other cruising families checking-in on Sunday morning. In spite of the hustle and bustle, we were still warmly greeted and served by cheerful Alessandro and Francesca. Throughout our stay, they were both anxious to assist us and tend to our needs and questions. We had booked a deluxe room and declined an upgrade to a beautiful suite next door, mainly because we wanted the convenience of being close to the breakfast dining area inside the hotel. We had room 112, which faces the Grand Canal. The vaparettos started running about at about 6:30 am but their noise did not really disturb us from sleeping (but, our windows were closed). The hotel does have a modern elevator/lift and the breakfast at 5 euros per person is one of the best deals in Venice. There is a small bar area adjacent to the lobby where we had coffee/tea on two occasions. Internet is complimentary in the lobby and it was very fast.We thought that the hotel's location was fine, given it's proximity to the vaporetto stop (across the canal), an easy 5 minute walk across the Scalzi Bridge. There are a number of restaraunts within easy walking distance. Also, we took a free shuttle bus from the cruise terminal to the Piazzale Roma. Plan on about a 10 minute hike from there to the hotel with luggage. We wished that the two bridges between the hotel and the Ple Roma had ramps on them! To get to the airport, use the B2 bus for 6 Euro per person-the ticket office is across the street from the Piazzale at the bus terminal. It was about a 30 minute ride on the bus to the airport. Venice is a wonderful city and our stay at the Antiche Figure was definitely one of the highlights.

<Author>WerdnaTrips
<Content>I'd recommend to anyone! A very well situated hotel run by staff who are genuinely willing and happy to help you.Upon arrival we were given the option of upgrading to a suite which we were shown, but these are not directly connected to the main hotel, instead you walk a short way down the side of the hotel to another block. The suites were immaculate and contain their own kitchen areas if required. These were a little beyond our price range however so we opted for a room within the hotel itself, again, very well prepared and lovely decor, typical Venetian style. Our room was not directly overlooking the grand canal, but this could be seen from the bedroom window. With the window open you can hear the hustle and bustle of Venetian life, with them shut - not a sound.The staff were superb. Any questions you have about Venetian transport or tourist attractions you should ask the staff first! Also they were very useful in suggesting places to eat (off the tourist trail) and we never had a bad meal.Being on the grand canal, close to the bus/train depot but away from the expensive St. Marks Square region was ideal. Hardly any dragging of suitcases around Venice is needed and a short ride on the water bus gets you to the main attractions.Highly recommended.

<Author>valueaddedCanada
<Content>Excellent service Wonderful place. Add kind and patient to the glowing reports for front desk personnel. Here is some extra info:1. Booked 3 superior rooms 5 months in advance via hotel website and expedia for pre-cruise stay. Our rooms on the 2nd. 3rd and 4th floors appeared exactly as shown on website. Very firm beds. Adequate size for us. Anyone over 6'2 and 300 lbs might find the superior rooms a tad small. Walls are padded to reduce noise. There is a lift. Guests may use one computer in lobby for free internet access. TV has English language news channel.2. Breakfast is included with room rate if booked via website but cost 5 euros ( a bargain) if booked on expedia. Ask server to make you a cappucino (no extra cost) or use the coffee machine.3. Arrived via blue bus from Marco Polo airport to Piazzale Roma (bus terminal) in the pouring rain. Bus terminal is an open-air bus stop, not a building. Cheap plastic rain ponchos are assets during the rainy season. 4. To get to hotel by foot from Piazzale Roma, look for the white stone bridge or the green metal bridge directly in front of the terminal exit. The exit is lined with small souvenir shops. There is a public WC. The bridges cross the Rio Nuovo (small canal) and consists of about 40 to 50 steps (no ramp). Once you cross either bridge, the Grand Canal will be on your left hand side (you can't miss it). Keep walking along the Grand Canal. The hotel will be straight ahead. You need to cross another small bridge (about 30 steps) before reaching the hotel. The walk takes about 10 minutes, depending on how well you drag your cases over the bridges. We had 3 elderly travellers who were able to negotiate the step bridges with their cases with assistance.4. To get to hotel by vaporetto (public water bus) or water taxi: wouldn't recommend vaporetto. Too crowded. Water taxi stand is just steps from the terminal exit, along the Rio Nuovo, and takes you to a landing right in front of the hotel. Costly but worth it if you have mobility problems and lots of luggage.5. To get to the cruise port: there are two cruise ship ports. find out which one you need. Ask front desk about sharing water taxi to the port. Elderly members of our group rebelled against walking back to Piazzale Roma to catch free port shuttle. Shared taxi fare with 7 passengers- total cost of 110 euros (about 16 euros per person) to Stazione Marittima. We were met at the port's water taxi landing by cruise staff who efficiently handled our cases.

<Author>Gerta01
<Content>Perfect Location in Venice - Michele ROCKS! We would recommend this hotel to ANYONE and EVERYONE traveling to Venice. Since we came in by train and available transportion in Venice is by boat or on foot, the location couldn't be more perfect. Not only is the termini an excellent reference point to always find your way back to the hotel, if you have heavy bags as we did, your only challenge is hauling luggage up and down the steps of the bridge!Michele was an excellent host and local resource for us. He recommended two wonderful restaurants which we enjoyed each night of our stay and Antiche Figure had a warm and inviting atmosphere. They are not kidding when they describe the balcony as small but having the view of the Canal and large windows to enjoy the canal activity and landscape of Venice was an excellent treat.A cautionary word for travelers interested in visiting Murano. One of the things that I really wanted to do while in Venice was a visit to a Murano glass factory. The front desk informed us that we could arrange a private pick up from outside of our hotel and the driver would take us directly to Murano, free of charge. If you are into handsome Italian men, this place is for YOU. Our Italian Stallion ushered us into the factory to watch a SHORT demonstration of glass blowing by a master (who was drinking beer at 10:30am inbetween demonstrations and seeking tips for his 5 minutes of work). Then we were escorted into the show room where a well-dressed 50-something man invited us to look around and choose something that we like without worring about cost. Although we chose a piece to remember our honeymoon trip, it felt a little like lambs to the slaughter. This became extremely evident when it was recommended that instead of returning to Venice right away, we should make our next stop (another free boat ride) Burano where they make lace. We only had 3 days/2 nights in Venice and didn't realize that this excursion would require 4+ hours. Burano is beautiful and we would say that this is worth the time if you have time. However, if you are limited and enjoy history and the landscape of Venice, we would suggest sticking with the cultural highlights and save Murano/Burano for a longer visit to Venice.

<Author>Technical-Rose
<Content>Perfect Stay Traveled through Italy during October and, yes, everything is expensive compared to American standards. So, we try not to break the bank so we can travel more often.Antiche Figure is a small hotel in Venice directly across the canal from the train station. It took us maybe 5 minutes to walk there. Don't waste the time or money on a water taxi. Keep in mind that the bridges have steps, not ramps.The room was cute and probably a normal size for a European hotel. The front rooms are suites and face the canal. Ours was off to the side but we could still see the canal well. Breakfasts were standard fare: cereal, pastries, fruit, hard-boiled eggs, cold cuts, coffee, tea, juice, etc. The staff is very nice and language is not a problem. There is a lounge on the first floor where guests would sometimes gather in the evening for a drink or just conversation. I think a major plus for this area is that it is on high enough ground where there is no flooding during high tide. We could tell who got flooded by where the elevated walkways were placed.All in all, we had a wonderful time, even in the rain. If returning to Venice, I would definitely stay at this hotel again.

<Author>croesio
<Content>An excellent hotel located on Grand Canal We booked this hotel after reading reviews on Tripadvisor and we werenot disappointed. The assistant manager, Gianni, was very helpful throughout our short stay.I am not going to repeat all of the great comments but add some that we found very helpful on our visit.We arrived in the dark and after settling in Gianni directed us to a lovely, local restaurant, very close to the hotel, where we were able to eat (shuts at 11pm).Our booking did not include breakfast but because we had booked through expedia breafast was only 5 Euros instead of the normal 15 Euros. There was ample to eat:- cereals, yoghurts, cheese, ham, boiled eggs etc. Coffee was from a machine but it was fine. The hotelalso runs a free water taxi to and from the island of Murano where you can visit the glass factory.Our room did not have a canal view but we were shown rooms that did have this view. Nothing was too much trouble for the staff and they spoke excellent English.This is information that I found extremely helpful when arriving in Venice.1. After picking up your luggage turn left in Airport entrance and buy a 30Euro 3 day pass for the water buses (vaperetto) and the airport bus. This pays for itself after day 1.2. This info was given to me by another trip advisor member but it was so handy. Take the number 5 bus from the airport to the Piazzale Roma (the main bus station). This takes about 25 minutes, runs every half hour and the 3 day pass covers the fare. Stamp your ticket in the orange box when you get on the bus. When you get off the bus, go straight ahead, down the steps towards the canal. Turn left, cross the bridge, turn left and then cross another bridge. The hotel is now only a short walk away. 3. If you have a short stay ,use a day to visit the islands in the lagoon. The hotel taxi service will take you to Murano, then you can use your 3 day pass to go to Burano. This is a must. A beautiful island which makes lace. The houses are all brightly coloured. Plentyof places to eat. From there a short hop to Torcello where you can see Venices oldest cathedral. Beautiful mosaics. Then back to Burano and the on to San Marco (St Marks Square). Allow a day. The journeys take longer than you expect. Enjoy Venice. We did and we would returnto same hotel.

<Author>SWB_7
<Content>Friendly Antiche Figure We have just returned from a 3-night stay at the Hotel Antiche Figure in Venice, and were extremely impressed wirh the Hotel. It is situated on the Grand Canal, and is within easy reach of bus and train stations, as well as being close to vaporetta stops, making it easy to get around Venice. The staff were very friendly and helpful, and we were always greeted with a smile. When we arrived at the hotel, a member of staff gave us a map, and spent about 10 minutes giving us useful information, such as how to use the local transport, things to do and see, and where to eat. As a result, we were able to make the most of our stay in Venice, and felt very comfortable about asking for information as and when we needed it.The hotel itself was stylishly decorated, clean, warm (the weather was quite cold when we visited Venice, so if you go in October like we did, take jumpers, scarves and gloves, as well as a good coat and sensible shoes!), and there was a good variety of fresh food for breakfast. We were upgraded to a newly refurbished room, with a canopied bed, and an ensuite with a power shower with side jets of water - very sumptuous, and romantic. The room had all the facilities we needed, including a safe, hairdryer and minibar. There were fresh towels , and even sweets on the pillows every day. Attention to detail, with Italian style and hospitality, is what made this hotel a real winner. We had a lovely time, and would certainly recommend it.Tips: Make sure you take mosquito repellant, and those plug-in things, as mosquitos are rife in Venice, and be aware that eating out can be quite expensive. A great restaurant to eat in is the Alla Madonna, on Calle Alla Madonna, close to the Rialto bridge, where the food is amazing - but get there early, as there are often queues to get in. (Opens at 6.45pm) Also, if you are staying for a few days, it is a good idea to buy a local transport ticket, which you can use on the vaporetta around Venice, and the bus service to and from the airport . We were hopping on and off the Vaporetta a lot, and we reckon it saved us a lot of money. (We paid 30 Euros each for a 72 hour ticket, but it paid for itself in the first day.) Also be aware that Venice can flood occasionally, making it difficult to get around. It wasn't too bad while we were there, but we could see that it could get quite tricky in places if there were exceptionally high tides. The locals put up raised wooden walkways when flooding occurs, which partially solve the problem, but could be difficult for some people to climb on to. There is so much to see, so plan your itinerary carefully. Hope you have as fabulous a time as we did.  
<Date>Oct 27, 2007

<Author>Mgt 101
<Content>Little gem on the Grand Canal We stayed at the Antiche Figure for four nights in September. We booked this hotel in Venice because of the excellent Tripadvisor reviews and we were not disappointed. The Antiche Figure is excellently located both for the bus and train stations. Having seen people lugging cases around in Venice looking for their accomodation on this occasion and on previous occasions, believe me that is a a major plus for the hotel. The hotel is also across (bridge nearby) the canal from the Vaporetto stop so access to the Rialto and St Mark's is very easy. It is also a fairly reasonable walk if you feel up to the 20-25 minutes or so it takes.The hotel is very clean, beautifully decorated and we upgraded to a beautiful room overlooking the canal. The staff were most pleasant and helpful in relation to directions, travel, advice on dining etc.A few pieces of advice 1) the three day vaporetto ticket is a great deal2) if you have time take the No 1 from Piazzale Roma to the end of the line, it is a great way to orient yourself3) go to Burano, it is a picturesque island and the trip across is very pleasantWhen I return to Venice it will definitely be to the Antiche Figure.

<Author>ChicTravelerAlberta
<Content>This place is fabulous! The Hotel Antiche Figure is fully deserving of the praise it receives on this site. We thought the location was ideal - if you are carrying even a little bit of luggage, the steps and bridges of Venice can be a nightmare. Antiche Figure is steps away from the train station - cross one bridge and there you are. It is also close to some wonderful parts of Venice that are less touristy, such as Santa Croce.We had a lovely room with a canal view. The room was done in a classic Venetian style and looked pretty glam overall. We had no problems with canal noise, as the windows are likely soundproofed and had substantial shutters. The bathroom was spacious. There was plenty of closet space and a large desk in the room. They serve breakfast in a very nice dining area just off of the lobby. The made dinner reservations for us, and then re-arranged them to accommodate the changes in weather so we could dine outside. One staff member actually remembered where we were having dinner one evening and took the time to ask us about it. They were also excellent about providing directions, which is a much needed service in a place like Venice. As we were checking out on our way to Florence, another member of the hotel staff gave us dining suggestions and even a few menu choices! These people are a class act.I would absolutely stay at Antiche Figure again - bravo!

<Author>hughesphx
<Content>Wonderful small Hotel with a view We stayed at the Antiche Figure for 2 nights after a 12 night cruise. I booked the Antiche Figure for it's proximity to the Piazzale Rome (bus terminal). We got a bus ride from the port terminal to the Piazzale and walked with our bags (over 2 bridges) to the Hotel. It was a fairly easy walk even with 2 large bags and 3 carry on size bags. We had a canal view room on the third floor and it was breathtaking. The view up and down the Grand Canal was all I expected. There is some noise from the boats on the canal but with the windows closed it was not noticeable. The buzz on the Grand Canal was part of the Venice experience, in my opinion. The water taxi is just across the canal and St. Mark's square is an easy 30-45 minute walk. The directions from the front desk are easy to follow and the walk is very worthwhile for the shopping and dining. This area of Venice is less crowded with tourists and has more local flavor than the area around St. Marks. When leaving, we walked back to the bus terminal and took a blue airport bus for 3 euros. (Beats the water taxi prices). The breakfast for 5 euros is very basic but still not bad considering the cost of breakfast elsewhere in Venice.

<Author>csquared1030
<Content>Wonderful hotel, friendly and helpful staff We stayed in the Hotel Antiche Figure for 3 nights in a room on the fourth floor overlooking the Grand Canal. Not only were we warmly greeted by the desk clerk, Francesca, but we were shown two rooms on different floors to choose for our stay. Suggest travelers to Venice pack light if walking to their hotel.
