<Author>Patagonia8
<Content>Hotel Antiche Figure is the place to stay!! The Hotel Antiche Figure is a small lovely hotel with a great location at a quieter end of the Grand Canal and perfectly located to take the vaparetto to go where ever you want (get a 3 day pass and you save money). I don't think you could find a lovelier hotel with rooms facing the Grand Canal even if you were to spend mega dollars. The fact that you look across at the unattractive train station is mediated by having a room that faces the Grand Canal and seeing all the action that takes place on the Canal. The airconditioning is excellent.The major downside is that there is no internet available in the hotel and the internet cafe has unbearably slow processing which really means no internet while you are in Venice. We just returned from staying there 7 nights and were delighted to be there. All of the staff is delightful. The breakfast is adequate (5 Euro when you book with Expedia) but there is nothing hot like eggs or really good Italian cheese, etc. Take your food to the outside tables overlooking the canals! We were thrilled to have chosen this hotel!A trip advisor member, Los Angeles, CA.

<Content>Fabulous hotel Fantastic little hotel. It was convenient for all forms of transport. In a vibrant, yet not too noisy part of the city. Hotel staff were extremely friendly and helpful. <Author>Grumpathome
<Content>Perfect small hotel on the Grand Canal with great customer service! I am going to sum up this review first, then if it still interests you, you can read the rest: : If you are looking for a Big American style hotel - then Antiche Figure is not for you. But if you want a charming boutique style hotel with clean comfortable accomodations, the charm of Venice, Murano glass fixtures, a great location to explore Venice from and incredibly friendly customer service (with excellant English) then the Antiche Figure is for you !I need to start by telling you about booking our rooms. I read all the reviews in TA before emailing Antiche Figure - all the reviews that raved about this hotel were right. Customer service began with the emails we exchanged. I was booking rooms for 10 people and was trying to make everyone happy, Antiche Figure did. Not only did Alessandro answer all my questions about the hotel and its' accommodations, but he answered lots of questions about Venice. He could not have been any more helpful! Also check out their website for lots of pictures and their email address.My family stayed here in the middle of July after a cruise ending in Venice. We had 4 rooms, (3 doubles and one quad). They were all nicely decorated, with comfortable beds (they even have kings), very clean, with working air conditioning, nice bathrooms and a fridge ( it was stocked, but we were told we could move stuff to make room for our water bottles). The hotel is wonderful, in a wonderful location, especially if you want to get away from the noise and tourists around San Marco. There is even a lovely patio with tables in front of the hotel where you can sit and enjoy the gondolas etc. on the Grand Canal.It is a 5 min. walk from Piazzale Roma ( we had a lot of luggage, but were able to to get over the two walking bridges with a little extra effort - it is still easier to walk to the Antiche Figure than to get to most hotels in Venice. You can also leave your luggage at the P. Roma where there is a boat that will deliver it to the hotel for several Euros a bag - but the walk was not too bad. The hotel is also across the canal from the train station. It is also near a waterbus stopWe went to the hotel to check it out on our first day in Venice ( we had one night on ship and then disembarked the next morning). Alessandro helped us with maps, directions, suggestions about where to go and where to get lunch - and we weren't even checking in until the next day. We arrived the next morning around 8:30 AM (the ships gets you off early) with at least 24 bags, since it was still early and the rooms were not ready, Alessandro helped us stack all our bags next to the desk in the lobby, this is a small hotel with a small lobby so we took up a lot of space. He arranged a free taxi to take us to a glass factory in Murano. The factory and showroom were great and not high pressure, but I decided to keep looking at other shops, so I passed on purchasing a bowl that I liked, since I thought we might see something similar for less money elsewhere. We shopped some more in Murano, then took a waterbus back. I had not found anything I liked better and regretted not buying it and told Francesca about it at the front desk, she offered to get another water taxi to take me back to the glass factory, but since it was late, I did not want to do that, she called the factory for me, found out which salesman had helped me, I talked to him and with some faxing back and forth, I was able to order my murano glass and have it shipped to the USA. ( he had quoted me a price before we left that morning - he remembered the bowl as the one he was trying to give to me....) this was another example of how helpful and nice they are at AF! When we returned, all our bags were in the right rooms - a real feat, since most ot them had the same last name. That evening we were able to walk from AF to the Ponte Vecchio in about 15 - 20 mins. with lots of shopping and browsing on the way. To get to San Marco, you can waterbus or walk it in about 30 mins. Walking in Venice is a must! Lots of interesting little streets, but signs on the corner of building to point you in the right direction. The breakfast is served in two small rooms and was a nice little buffet with enough choices to fill you up. Everything was fresh and nicely displayed.Overall we could not have picked a better place to end our cruise of the Mediterranean and we will go back! Kudos to Alessandro and Francesca for all their help!  
<Date>Aug 19, 2006

<Author>cornbread35
<Content>Right on the Grande Canal We arrived in Venice early in the morning after a Ryanair flight from Rome ($4.95 on-line sale- see more below). The flight goes into Treviso Airport, so you have a 5 Euro, 45 minute bus ride to the Piazza Roma in Venice. As noted in other reviews, the Antiche Figure is a quick 5 minute walk from the bus station, although I will note that you do have to carry your bags over two bridges. Our room was not yet ready, but reception was very accomidating and took care of our bags and gave us maps and hints to start our exploration of the area. When we returned mid afternoon, our room was ready, on the top floor in the corner, so we had three windows overlooking the Grande Canal. No balcony, but the view was really neat. The room was very, very nice. One quirky thing I had never seen before was a key card slot near the door to operate the lights in the room. They had not told us about that at check in, and we could not at first figure out why the light in the room did not work. Then I saw the key slot on the wall by the door, inserted my room key and all the lights came on. We had planned to get a waterbus pass for our time in Venice, but after that first day we realized with a good map, knowing your primary end destination (i.e. San Marco) and willing to make a few wrong turns, you can travel the city pretty well on foot, so we skipped the water bus passes. Venice streets were very crowed, but it appeared that so were the water busses. I did not give this hotel an excellent rating, as my wife and I agreed that the breakfast, which was included, was only so so. The juice was only red juice, the coffee came from a push button machine and was not very good, and the food selection was pretty bland. Breakfast did not compare favorably at all to the other places we stayed in Italy during out trip. We took a gondola ride from one of the boats right in front of the hotel. We went about 5 o'clock and they were not particularly busy. It was 80 euro for 40 minutes or 120 euros for an hour. He showed us on a map what the difference was, and we did the hour. Even though they start in the Grande Canal, you soon get off the busy routes and into the smaller, more intimate canals. Our gondalier was pleasant, informative and made our ride very memorable. I had read horror stories about grouchy operators, but when we noticed the lines of people waiting near St Marks for rides, it was no wonder. Our operator said that he knows that he could make more money if he took over his father's permit at St. Marks, but he prefers to take life a little slower.RyanAir- By taking a 7 a.m. flight to Venice we were at our hotel by 9:30 a.m. vs. a 6 hour drive in the car. For others in the U.S., RyanAir is like Southwest without the frills(?). They are full size jets, but fly from regional airports. You take a bus from the terminal to your jet on the tarmac. I had never heard of them, but would not hesitate to fly them again if I needed an economy flight.

The rooms were large and clean but the bathroom had mould, it wasn't bad but I was surprised by that for a æ‹¢150 a night deluxe room. Overall it wasn't a bad hotel at all and not one to complain about but I definitely expected more following these reviews so was left feeling a bit disappointed and probably wouldn't stay there again.

<Author>WAgal
<Content>Our whole family loved it Our family (10 of us, 4 rooms) stayed overnight after a cruise which ended in Venice. The staff was outstanding, esp. <Content>Great hotel, unforgettable stay Date: 9-10 July 2006.Our family of four (two teenagers) stayed at the hotel for two magnificent nights. The bar of the hotel is, supprisingly, cheaper than most cafeterias and bars in the city and definitely with a better view.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Absolutely wonderful We have just returned from a 6 night stay with friends (Woodley). After our visit last year we made a promise to return, not only to Venice, but to The Hotel Antiche Figure. All of the staff were helpful and very informative. Being situated opposite the railway station makes the hotel ideally appointed, as it is not right in the middle of all that goes on! however you will not be disappointed as life seems to carry on throughout the night, but after a few beers and a very good malt you won't hear a thing.The standard of the hotel cannot be faulted, it is clean, the rooms are of a generous size, and I would thoroughly recommend spending that little bit extra to book the rooms overlooking the Grand Canal, You will NOT be disappointed!If I was pressed to make any complaint it would only be that tea making facilities would be a bonus. I suppose only an Englishman could make such a comment, but that first cup in the morning reallly needs to be before breakfast!!And do please ask the hotels advice with regards as to where to eat, you will not be disappointed and you will not be ripped off as you could well be if you are attracted by the bright lights of the canal and the persuavive patter of some of the other restaurants close by!Enjoy your stay at the Hotel Antich Figure, perhaps we might meet you there as we will bet returning.

<Author>Monty-Basset
<Content>Fantastic We have just returned from 6 days at the Hotel Antiche Figure in Venice. Friends had warned us not to return to the same place/hotel (we first stayed there last year and liked it so much that we had booked again for this year) as they are never as good as you remember - they could not have been more wrong. This time we had booked the rooms overlooking the Grand Canal and it was worth every penny. In addition, the hotel and the staff were just as good as we remembered, if not better.The hotel is ideally situated right on the Grand Canal close to all facilities, bridge, train, bus (water and auto), water taxi and gondola stations are all within easy reach. A lot of hotels claim to be on the canal, which they are, but not the Grand Canal, so be careful.The Hotel Antiche Figure provides an excellent continental spread at breakfast time and although they do not provide evening meals this is not a problem as there are plenty of excellent restaurants close by, but be sure to ask the staff which they recommend, and be sure to follow their advice.

<Author>citi-tripper
<Content>Great Hotel - Glad we took your advice ! We stayed at the Hotel AF for 4 nights at the beginning of June 2006 (2 adults + teenage son) and we can highly recommend it. The hotel itself is small but spotlessly clean with very hard working staff who make you feel very welcome. We met Alessandro the manager and Francesa who gave us lots of advice to make our trip enjoyable. We had an excellant room (211) with a large double and a single bed, large marble bathroom and small balcony. We really enjoyed watching the world go by from the balcony - either standing on it or sitting in our room at the open balcony door with our feet up after a hard days sight seeing. The mini bar prices for water (2 euro) beer (4 euro) were about 80 cents higher than in shops but a cold beer in the comfort of your own room was worth it. We saw other hotels that we had been tempted to book but were very relieved that we hadn't as none of them had a prime spot on the grand canal like the AF, so our advice is to look no further than this hotel. It's location by the bus / train stations is ideal and despite being on the canal side once the shutters were closed at night there was no noise preventing a good nights sleep - especially after a lovely hot chocolate in the bar.We booked direct through the hotel's web site having checked tripadvisor reviews and exchanged friendly emails with Gianni before our visit. Breakfast was very good and at busy times guests sat in the bar area or outside to eat and the staff worked very hard to keep up with demand (and always with a smile).Our favourite restaurant was Marciana, in Calle Lunga Chioverette. Turn right out of the hotel walk to the Scalzi bridge; do not cross the bridge but turn right again at the bridge and it is the second restaurant on the right. The waiter Leon was very friendly and amusing and I had a complimentary cocktail for my birthday.Top tips.When arriving at the airport, do not stand in a long queue / line at the window marked public transport, but walk past to the tourist information desk where without waiting we bought bus tickets to Venice (the No 5 at 2 euros) and a three day vaporetto pass that will take you anywhere on the water as often as you like. Gondolas extra (but you have to do it!!). Outside hotel the price was 80 euros.Forget Murano and the Lido!!!DO visit Burano with it's pretty painted houses.DO book the secret tour of the Doges Palace through the hotel. You will miss very long queues and actually see far more of the palace!Wandering around Venice can be a challenge, but DO try it. Many Calles end in a canal with no bridge or a dead end. You will make friends with other lost souls. Just follow the signs to 'Ferrovia' and you WILL be fine.We have never written a review before, but on this occasion felt we had to join others in recommending this lovely hotel and say thank you for the advice from other reviewers.  
<Date>Jun 20, 2006

<Content>Absolute Perfection!!! we stayed at the beautiful Antiche Figure Hotel for 2 nights, May 23 and 24. I had been so excited to stay at this hotel, and was not disappointed! <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Excellent Location! My husband and I stayed at the Antiche Figure for three nights in early May. Our room was on the first floor (one above street level) , was quite large and overlooked the canal. It's a busy location, so if you don't like street noise (voices, laughter, gondolas - no cars!) ask for a room either higher up or off the canal. The location across the canal from the train station was great - except for lugging our bags up the bridge stairs. Oh well. The staff was great - Francesca especially. Breakfast was fine, except for the coffee from the automatic machine in the dining room. AVOID IT if you consider yourself a coffee lover. Ask the staff to make you an espresso or americano from the real machine at the bar. Trust me. Oh, and try the little cafe down the alley adjacent to the hotel - the cafe right next to the laundry facility. They make excellent sandwiches!

We had booked the famous blue room with balcony and it was a joy to behold. With marvellous views overlooking the Grand Canal, it was very spacious with lots of storage spaces and a beautiful and spotless marble bathroom.The breakfast was the usual continental style, but the young lady who ran the breakfast room was so kind and gave a warm and individual welcome every morning. She ran the place like clockwork and was so efficient and we began to think could this place get any better. It did. Unfortunately my wife was ill for a day or two during our stay, but the staff arranged for a doctor to visit her at the hotel. We obviously had to pay for this ourselves, but it was the kind and understanding way in which the staff assisted us which I will never forget. A lesser hotel might not want to know about your problems.As if that wasnt enough to recommend this hotel, the location was excellent. A short two minute walk over Scalzi bridge and you're at the St Lucia Train Station. During our stay we travelled to Milan, Florence and Vicenza on day trips and the close proximity to the station meant that we had lots more time to relax at our destination. Arriving back from Florence at 11.30pm, we were sipping a gorgeous hot chocolate at the bar in our hotel at 11.35pm!There are many fine restaurants (and an Irish bar) within a few footsteps of the hotel. I would recommend Gino's on the Rio Terra Lista di Spagna. They do a marvellous Pizza Calzone. St. Marks Square and Rialto Bridge are about a 20 minute walk from the hotel, but walking is the only true way to experience this city. Our trip was truely memorable and this was in no small part to the wonderful hotel. We will definately be returning to this hotel in near future.  
<Date>May 20, 2006

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>What a Hotel 8 of us have just returned from the Hotel after 4 days of of an excellent experience. The hotel was brilliantly situated on the Grand Canal opposite the railway station and the Ferrovia Water Bus stop which made travelling around easy. there was also a gondola station outside the hotel which made sitting outside with a drink after a long day very interesting. The rooms were nicely decorated with chandaliers in the room and even in the bathroom. You could pay extra for a Canal view but we didn't bother. We enjoyed a lovely breakfast each morning for which we paid 5 Euros as Expedia travellers consisting of cold meat, cheese, boiled eggs, pastries, tea, coffee and orange juice. The staff were very friendly and nothing was too much trouble. Whilst not in the main area of venice this was quite nice as you could get away from the larger crowds. We shall certainly be recommending this hotel to our friends and booking again in the near future.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A lovely little hotel Prior to moving into an apartment for a week, we spent a night in the Hotel Antiche Figure in Venice. It is located on the Grand Canal, across from the train station, admittedly not the most charming view, which may account for its price being more reasonable.It does make it easy to find and handy if you will be taking trains. Our room was small, but attractive with a fine bathroom and closet space. The breakfast was typical of our experience with Italian hotel breakfasts; baked goods, fruit, cereal, slices of ham and cheese, etc. There was a neat self-service coffee machine from which you could get a selection of coffees. The desk staff spoke fabulous English, putting we Americans to shame. as usual. Allejandro (sp.?) made the phone call for us to contact the landlord of the apartment , a task I had been dreading . He also allowed us to store our luggage for several hours after we had checked out. As you leave the hotel take a left and walk into that pretty, less comercial area.This is a nice place to stay.

<Author>Itravl2
<Content>Great location in Venice Across the canal from the train station - you'd think it would noisy, butthe room was quiet, well-appointed, and very comfortable. The staff was top notch - emailed questions were answered sometimes withinan hour - when I phoned when we were in Italy already, the person whoI talked to said, when you get here, tell us what you want to do, and wewill help you make it happen. What more could you want? We were only there for two days in Venice, but had great meals at smallrestaurants (suggested by the hotel), had a great gondola ride (with agondolier who was 4th generation, spoke good English, and knew anamazing amount of Venetian history), went to Murano, ate dessert in frontof St. Marco square (expensive, but very much part of the Venice experience),and still had time to people watch and wander around.We had an early morning flight out of Marco Polo airport - the hotel arrangeda taxi (the driver walked over to the hotel to help one of our group, who neededassistance, with their bag).The breakfast, which was included with the room, was good - pastries, freshfruit, cereal, yogurt, and assorted teas, juices, and coffees. We splurged for this last hotel on our trip and had their best rooms on the top floorfacing the canal, still not as expensive as staying at many other hotels. It was agreat, comfortable, relaxing place to finish our 2 week trip to Italy. We hope toreturn to Venice and the Hotel Antiche Figure for a longer stay in the future.

<Author>safa_in_England
<Content>Believe all the reviews I'm a tripadvisor fan and use it to decide on hotels around the world. It proved itself again in our choice of Hotel Antiche Figure for the May 1 long weekend. The hotel is lovely, it's location is excellent and its staff very helpful. We arrived a day late to the hotel, after BA cancelled our flight the previous night. When we arrived the staff were very apologetic (although it clearly wasn't their fault), and offered us free breakfast for the remainder of our stay (our expedia rate did not include breakfast) to make up for the lost day. To get to the hotel take the bus from the airport to the bus terminal in Venice. It only costs 2 euro's per person and it's only a 5 min walk from the bus terminal to the hotel. Would definately recommend this hotel.

<Author>DowningUk
<Content>A gem of a hotel My husband and I got back late last night from a two night stay in Venice on 9th and 10th April using this hotel. Venice exceeded our expectations - and the hotel made our stay extra special. Well done to all the staff at Hotel Antiche Figure for reaching No 1 in Tripadvisor!Location - excellent as it is a 5 min walk from coach station at Piazzale Roma, opposite the train station, adjacent to the Ponte d Scalzi Bridge (one of the three bridges to cross the Grand Canal) and opposite the Ferrovia waterbus stop.Hotel - extremely well maintained, spotlessly clean, excellent decor and furnishings throughout. We arrived on an early flight, and as a room had already been cleaned, it was made available to us early so we were able to settle in, freshen up and go straight into Venice. We had a red room to the rear on the 4th floor, which had a lovely view of the Grand Canal.Staff - they were all extremely welcoming, polite and helpful. The hotel receptionist booked the Ducale Palace secret tour for us (which is well worth visiting).Breakfast - this is provided in two small beautifully decorated rooms. Plenty of choice ie: rolls, ham, cheese, cereal, croissants, muffins, eggs, yoghurts, orange juice and coffee/tea etc.Recommendations - use the vaporetta (waterbuses) - buy the tickets at the booths entering the main landing stages ie: Ferrovia (single fare E5, 24 hr ticket E12, 72 hr ticket E25) and pickup a timetable. Don't just stick to main sights ie: Piazza San Marco (St Marks), Rialto Bridge etc, but meander the back streets by foot. We also took the waterbus to other islands ie: Burano (famous for lace and has wonderfully coloured houses), and Murano (famous for glass blowing). We used a local restaurant recommended by the hotel which was very nice, and also a restaurant using their tourist menu which was good value for money.

<Author>Charlie-Sam
<Content>Best Hotel in Venice All the reviews are spot on. The hotel is in a perfect location. Great rooms, friendly staff and close to lots of good restaurants.Being opposite one of only 3 bridges that crosses the Grand canal and a main Vaporetto stop it is very easy to explore Venice from this hotel. <Author>vibiaron
<Content>Great especially for late night arrival at Santa Lucia The reviews don't lie - this hotel is really a find. The location is great - it's literally across the Grand Canal from the Santa Lucia train station. We had a red room (not a canal view) and it was quite small, but clean and charming. The bathroom had all the amenities and was really nice for a 3-star hotel.One world of caution, though. While it is literally steps from the station, it's the steps you need to keep in mind. To get over the canal, you need to go over a bridge that is all steps up and down. If you're over 50 and you're carrying a small suitcase and a tote bag, you'll be puffing by the time you get to the other side. I think it was worth it.We arrived at 8:30 p.m., checked in, dropped our bags, and went to find a pizzeria. That in itself is a typically Venetian adventure at night. To keep your bearings, just keep looking up to follow the signs for Rialto and make sure that the Grand Canal (the water) is always on your left. The rooms have high-speed internet access, but you must remind them when you check in to enable it. Also, the ethernet jack in our room was behind the TV armoire which we had to move to find. The gentleman who checked us in forgot to mention that little tidbit!We took the ATVO bus from the Piazzale Roma (10 min. walk with luggage and 2 bridges - remember the steps) to Marco Polo the next morning. CAUTION: You must buy your ticket for this bus in the ticket office at the plaza before you board the bus. The only time they allow you to buy your ticket on the bus is when the office is closed. We found out the hard way, although the driver very kindly and patiently waited for us (and about 5 other unaware tourists) to run and buy the tickets at the office. Imagine an American bus driver doing that!

<Author>elaine-7
<Content>wonderful! Just returned from a wonderful stay in venice- made all the more perfect with the Hotel Antiche Figure! What more can i add to what has already been written - the views onto the grand canal from our 4th floor room were amazing! Service was impecable. It is well worth paying the five euro for breakfast if you book with expedia; lots of choice and it really sets you up for the day ahead. Highlights of the trip for us were St Marks Square (obviously), The Basillica - although if you don't have a head for heights avoid climbing up to the balcony, my knees would not stop wobbling! Doge's palace was great for a rainy day. Do not miss Titian's Assumption of Mary in Santa Maria Gloriosa dei frari - it is truely a masterpiece! The Rialto Bridge is worth a photo opportunity but the crowds do get busy here, even in March. To get away from all the hustle and bussle of venice, a trip on the direct vaporetta to the islands of Murano, Burano and Torcello is recomended. A haven of peace and quiet but not too far away from all the action back in venice. Finally do not miss grabbing a front seat of the vaporetta, (Numbers 1 or 82), sailing up the grand canal with a birds eye view of venice laid out before you! - Fantastic!N.B don't bother with a map - they are useless,just follow the crowd and be prepared to get wonderfully lost!

<Author>Bart_ollie
<Content>Little Treasure We have just returned from a 3 night stay in Venice. I love Venice anyway but the Hotel Antiche Figure made the stay even more special. The hotel and rooms look immaculate as if only recently decorated. Our room had a huge comfortable bed and the bathroom was luxurious and spotless. Breakfast buffet was generous.All the staff were friendly and helpful and spoke excellent english.Recommend getting the 3 day bus pass as it doesn't matter if you get on the wrong boat occasionally as we did. Although generally all travel was really easy to understand including buses back to the airport. Just remember the hotel is opposite the railway station and you can't go wrong.We found the location good as it was easy to find when we arrived and easy to get to the airport from. It also overlooked the Grand Canal which was a bonus. It is a little way from the main attractions but nowhere is difficult to get to in Venice as the bus services are so good. Would recommend this hotel to anyone.

<Content>Five Star Treatment What a fantastic place! We booked with no real prior knowledge through Expedia. The bus from the airport cost a mere two Euros and dropped us just round the corner from this hotel. We received five star treatment ( in this three star hotel ). The desk staff were outstanding in their helpfulness and their recommendation of a local trattoria was so good we went there every evening. <Author>tostka
<Content>Loved the hotel We booked our first trip to Venice last December, and just arrived back from our trip last night. We booked 6 nights at Antiche Figure based completely on the high-praise for the hotel found in the posts here. Our experience is that AF is a stellar value. The day we arrived we were offered either a red room (on the side away from the Grand Canal) at our booked rate, a blue room (top floor front facing the canal, as a 25eur/day upgrade), or since we were staying so many days, the apartment the hotel owns. We took the top floor front blue room, so I have no details about the apartment, although other folks have mentioned it in these reviews. We simply decided that the original Pallazzo windows and longer/better view from the fourth floor sounded too good to pass up.*The hotel is incredibly convenient to the 3euro airport atvo-bus drop at Piazalla Roma (5mins walk down the canal to the landmark 'big green dome church' across the Grand Canal from the modern Ferrovia train station)*The room was spotless. *The bathroom was great: marble floors, walls, sizable tub with hand-shower. Nice modern fixtures. And of course the oft-mentioned beautiful murano crystal fixtures.*king-size bed (dbl-twin) mattresses).*mini-bar hidden in the desk (not cheap: 4euro cokes, but hey, it's extremely convenient and nothing in Venice is cheap :D)*a few foibles - not issues, as these aren't essential or even wanted items -- just differences compared to what you may see in western hotels: no alarmclock/radio (but wakeup calls are avail), no iron, no vending machines, no ice machine (that we saw). I mention these simply so that you can bring suitable items if you want them...*we booked through travelocity and the included continental breakfast was good. Nice array of options (croissants, meat, cheese, a nice rolled coffee cake,cereals,soft-boiled eggs in the shell, a variety of yogurts, etc...), all tasted very good, and you could eat as much as you wanted - no reason for anyone to go hungry. The lady policing the breakfast room was a pleasant blur of motion as she sailed around keeping the tables cleared  stocked. Yes the coffee from the machine is very strong, and be sure to use the 'stop' button to keep it from over-filling your cup.:D We got a table daily around 9:40am in the breakfast room. Except one day, when they had very few people checking out, all but two rooms booked and everyone decided to eat between 9  10 -- that was the only day that we actually saw they'd had to expand service to the tables out in the bar out front... We were there during the very slow period in Feb, but I could see where it could be a real scramble to get in for breakfast in July/Aug. Also, I can't for the life of me believe there's a review here from someone that sat in the breakfast room and waited for service. It's pretty clear it's a self-serve breakfast with several buffet tables of things to eat.*the staff is great. From management to the lady that cleaned our room. They were very interested in how happy we were, actively solicited ideas for improvements, and suggested several wonderful restaraunts when we asked. On serveral occasions they offered to make reservations for their recommendations.*When you're in Venice, USE THE VAPPRETTOS and available multi-day passes! We walked everywhere for five of the six days and my feet took a heck of a beating (still got the blisters to show for it). Not to mention, Venice can be a pretty tough town to navigate in on-foot, as the chains of signs leading you from Ferrovia (the landmark train station near hotel) to Rialto  S. Marco can be very easy to lose track of as you're navigating. We got solidly lost at least once a day -- found ourselves coming back to the hotel through the soon-all-too-familiar Cannaregio section instead of the shorter Rialto route, on several ocassions. It can get frustrating. The vapprettos are easy, fast, and largely fool-proof. Just sit down and watch things go by. Not to mention they're alot less excertion than hiking.:D*We loved Ostaria al Vecio Pozzo! Ended up eating there FOUR TIMES! We had some difficulty with book-recommended restaraunts all over town (all but one of the 7 we tracked down on foot from Rick Steves' 2006  Knopf Cityguide were permanently/seasonally closed). So whenever we got tired of tracking around town to restaraunts that may or may not be open, we just went to Vecio Pozzo! They always recognized us and greeted us warmly each visit. They've even got a web site with a large gallery of pictures, although it doesn't show the best part: the wonderful food or the people!: ---. Map at the site. As others have mentioned, it's a few blocks along the street on the right of the hotel, on Corte Canal # 656.*Another restaraunt recommended by the manager was Trattoria Antica Besseta. Very nice seafood, although the restaraunt was hard for us to find. We had both directions on our map (drawn by AF's manager) and a map on the back of the Besetta business card he gave us, and we still got completely lost and had to ask directions. 1395 Salizada de Cè„¿ Zusto (3-4 blks NE of the hotel). *Finally, another good spot from the Knopf Cityguide, that was open not very expensive and had great food, though not particularly close to the hotel, was Osteria Ai Assassini, in San Marco, On Rio Tera Dei Assassini, #3695 (several blks north of the Fenice Opera house off of Calle D. Verona).

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A good experience for us! I booked this hotel 3 months ago after reading good reviews on Tripadvisor and it lived up to all expectations. The room was excellent and the staff friendly and helpful.We splashed out and booked a canal view room for 4 nights and it was definitely worth it. Watching Venetian life pass by from our duel aspect 3rd floor room added an extra dimension to our holiday.Many hints and tips can be found in previous reviews but the ones I would particularly endorse include:Buying the 3 day waterbus ticket.The free trip to Murano by watertaxi (bookable at the hotel reception).Eating at the Ostaria al Vecio Pozzo a few minutes walk away (again, bookable at reception)If you're visiting the Doge's Palace consider buying a Museum ticket which will also give free access to other museums in the city. We spent an enjoyable (and inexpensive!) final day hopping on and off the vaporettos visiting those we had previously missed. Another invaluable tip was to follow the signs to Ferrovia (station) to find your way back to the hotel.Finally - we paid an extra 5 euros each for breakfast which was good value. I had read in previous reviews about the infamous coffee machine. I have to say it was fine for our morning tea but the coffee was not good! However,when I mentioned it on departure, I was informed by a member of staff that a freshly made coffee may be ordered and brought on request. So that's my main new tip to pass on to future guests!We very much enjoyed our stay at this hotel and would definitely recommend it to friends.

<Author>JohnandEileen
<Content>Could not fault this place.... Thank you to contributors to Tripadvisor - we booked this hotel for a long weekend in Venice in January and we really could not fault it. Don't be put off by the 3* superior rating, the price or the photos, it is excellent. Arriving into the bus station/railway station (can't stand the boarding scrum for Ryanair but that is another issue) go over the bridge, turn left along the canal, walk 100 metres and you are there. It is not the best end of the city, but you will be smiling watching the other passengers struggle to St Mark's Square. The hotel is warm and friendly. We booked a canal view room, which was exceptionally clean and comfortable. The marble bathroom was excellent and the whole place just looks new and well cared for. The staff were so helpful, booking restaurants and concerts for us and nothing was too much trouble. They also take a pride in maintaining standards and know how highly they are rated on Tripadvisor. I would have no hesitation recommending this hotel to anybody.Points to note - Expedia bookings do not include breakfast which is 5 euros and worth it. The view over the Grand Canal is mostly of the train station which isn't the prettiest view in Venice. You may get a little noise from the river buses but this quietens down at night and shouldn't put you off. You will also notice that the lift makes an annoying noise when it arrives but again these are only minor issues. If you want a reasonable break in Venice definitely book this place. Get the Time Out guide as it was briliant for restaurants, also get a 22 euro boat pass when you arrive which is great value. Take some very warm clothes if you go in January. If you can, avoid Treviso airport until they have built the new terminal - the current one is a joke!  
<Date>Jan 30, 2006

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Better than the Waldorf Astoria! Last weekend we arrived in a very cold and misty Venice, but what a warm welcome we got in hotel Antiche Figure! At the reception Alessandro patiently and kindly informed us about the hotel, breakfast etc. We had booked one of the spacious canal view rooms (blue room, nr. 211), preferably with balcony and so we got it! The room was beautifully furnished, very clean with excellent king size beds and a super luxurious marble bath room with Venetian chandeliers. We have also stayed at the Waldorf in NY, but the room we had there was not as well maintained as ours in Antiche Figure! The location of the hotel is also perfect: the vaporetto and railway station just in front. The area is more quiet but when you cross the bridge you are in a lively area with shops, restaurants etc., but not as expensive as in the San Marco area (E 10,-- for a sip of coffee, shame on them; please make sure you also double check the bill!!). We can really recommend this lovely hotel with very service minded staff: the breakfast lady (we think she's called Linda) fulfils are your breakfast wishes with pleasure, she's great and very hardworking. Unfortunately we missed Francesca, who was on a holiday. Gianni who helped us check-out was also a very service minded and kind guy and helped us efficiently with our transfer to the airport. We can highly recommend this lovely hotel and we would like to thank the wonderful staff and send them regards from Holland. We think Antiche Figure should be ranked no. 1 on Trip Advisor for Venice hotels! Josephine  Barbara

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Perfect hotel with which to end the Italy Grand Tour My husband and I just returned from an eight day trip through Italy and ended our stay at the Hotel Antiche Figure. The hotel, room, and staff were absolutely charming. All three of the front desk clerks we encountered spoke English very well and were wonderfully friendly and helpful, as was the woman who managed the breakfast area. Our room was just big enough, cozy, and clean. The bathroom was also spotless and a good size, relative to other hotels we have visited in Europe. The only thing that we saw that could be improved was the selection of food for breakfast. The food that was offered was good, but limited. However, I would note that the spread was pretty standard as compared to other hotels in Europe. The breakfast room itself was very spacious and clean.The location of the hotel was also extremely convenient for us since we arrived at Venice by train (the train station is right across the canal), we were able to catch a water bus to anywhere in Venice with a short three minute walk, and we departed Venice by plane (the main bus station with shuttles to the airport is a short 5 - 10 minute walk away). A tip to save some money: Buy the 22 Euro travel card from ACTV. It is good for 72 hours of unlimited trips on any of the ACTV water buses (including the Grand Canal water buses) and land buses (including the bus #5 to the airport).We would without a doubt return to this hotel on future trips to Venice.

I think after you do Saint Mark's square, feed the pigeons, and do the gondola, not sure what else there is to do. Of course we are two females (28 and 29), and not romantics, or honeymooning. We were looking to party and there was no partying to be had in Venice.Anyway, the location of this hotel CANNOT be beat, it was so nice to hop off the train (from Florence and Milan respectively), and cross the bridge and we are at our hotel. Of course we over packed and had to negotiate the stairs, but that's ok, we didn't have to hassle with the water taxi's or figure out the water bus schedules. That was great! I got to the hotel first and my room was ready on the first floor and we were pleasantly surprised. The use of a full length mirror with two females was very handy. Also, liked having the use of a safe in the room, and we loved the shower/tub combo, since this is rare. The location of the hotel is near restaurants and the concierge was very helpful and went above and beyond. They translated for us, when my girlfriend picked up a Milan soccer player that only spoke Italian; we only spoke English and some Spanish/French. Other than the concierge telling us he was a millionaire (NOT), she was a good sport about relaying messages. The b-fast was average, but this is a real deal and we booked it on Travelocity for like $125/night, so we were happy with our hotel choice. Thanks tripadvisor community, you got this one right.choice. Have fun!

<Author>Flyingmikewhisky
<Content>Charming Hotel My husband and I just got back from a weekend at the Hotel Antiche Figure, which we booked entirely on the basis of the reviews on Trip Advisor. We were delighted with the hotel and have no hesitation in recommending it very highly.It is small, intimate, decorated to a very high standard and has very helpful, charming, English-speaking staff.It is located on the side of the Grand Canal in Santa Croce, right next door to San Simeone Piccolo (large church with green dome). It is easily walked from either the train station (directly opposite the hotel via the Scalzi Bridge), or from the bus station in Piazzale Roma. If you are coming in from Marco Polo airport, take the blue ATVO bus (3 euro)which takes about 20 minutes. When you disembark the bus in Piazzale Roma, walk down the steps at the side of the Santa Chiara Hotel on to the banks of the Grand Canal. It's about a five minute walk (across two small bridges).The location is great, because you're not reliant on the vaporetto and a long walk before you get to your hotel. The restaurants recommended are cheaper and friendlier than those in the touristy areas around the Rialto bridge and San Marco.Just be prepared to walk a fair amount but we certainly felt that it was worth it, and we'd have no hesitation in going back to Hotel Antiche Figure!

<Author>PETPOP
<Content>Don't hesitate - book it! This is the ideal place to stay in Venice - a little away from the main tourist sites and the crowds but close enough to get to them easily and quickly by boat. The bus from Treviso airport stops 5 minutes walk away so there are just two small bridges to haul your luggage over - and the railway station is opposite if you come by train - again just 5 minutes walk over the Scalzi bridge. Your luggage can be stored if necessary after check out. There are plenty of quaint little alleyways, squares, shops, churches etc to explore [and get lost in!] close by after you have done the major sights.The view from the front [blue] rooms over the Grand Canal is well worth paying a bit extra for - the rooms are larger, not noisy, and watching the busy river traffic can be quite entertaining. We learned that the hotel was renovated and opened about three years ago - the rooms are spotless, very well equipped, comfortable and cosy with well designed quality fittings and fabric wallpaper [unmarked!] - even glass chandeliers over the two sinks in our large bathroom!Breakfast was certainly more than adequate - but there are no hot cooked eggs/bacon/sausage etc - previous writers comments have either been noted or expectations were too high.Staff are friendly - position is ideal - just note that there is no hotel lounge or restaurant so in bad weather the bar or your room is the only place to relax. Hence the three rather than five stars the hotel deserves. Thoroughly recommended!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Better than Wonderful! We had two nights in Venice before boarding our cruise ship. Looked on-line, saw the Hotel Antiche Figure reviews and booked our stay. We were six women in our 30's to 50's.From the airport we took a vapparetto (80 euros for us all including massive luggage) directly to the dock at the hotel. We were greeted on the dock by Alessandro the Manager, who quickly helped us with our luggage.Upon entering the hotel we were just knocked out by how beautiful the lobby and bar area were and how helpful Allesandro and his staff were. They answered every question we had (in English) and helped us with money exchange, telephone calls, restaurant recommendations, trips to Murano (the boat came and picked us up at the dock in front of the hotel). The entire staff goes out of their way to be helpful. Francesca (night manager) mentioned a wonderful restaurant that the locals love -- Ostaria al Vecio Pozzo -- a 5 minute walk around the corner from the hotel. The food was wonderful, the pace leisurely, and the staff very friendly and attentive.Our room was a canal view with balcony, third floor triple. The beds were all comfortable and the room was quiet and luxurious. The bathroom with all the marble and murano glass was georgous! The breakfast was great and it is included in the price of the room! I had a bit of trouble with the coffee machine, but the dining room server was happy to help me. The breakfast was more than we had expected...from cereals, yogurt, fruit, muffins, breads, to meats and cheeses. Trust me, we didn't go hungry.This should be listed as 5 star...it is beautiful, well run, and the staff is outstanding! When I return to Venice, I'm booking this hotel again.Barbara (and 5 lady friends)

<Author>jeromeoconnor
<Content>A small gem in a great city Contrary to the previous few nay-sayers, this lovely, small, and expertly maintained hotel is operated at the same high service level as the much more expensive hotels in this exceptional city. VERY professional and caring front desk, always ready to offer help, and among the best encountered anywhere by this former travel agent. The clean and recently renovated rooms are somewhat small by American standards, but perfectly adequate. The location near the Pizzalle Roma bus and rail stations may seem a negative, but is actually a benefit to those otherwise carrying baggage up and down the many bridges to hotels nearer the center. A nearby vaporetto stop brings all of Venice into easy reach. Fine restaurants nearby. Wonderful areas to stroll all around the hotel. Even the included breakfast is well done. Best of all is the price - at least 50% less that comparable hotels.

<Author>Sharonspud
<Content>Hotel Antiche Figure, Location is wonderful The Hotel Antiche Figure, what a wonderful location as it's only a 10 min walk from the bus station situated right by the Grand Canal, as you get off the coach at the bus station look along the canal for the church with the green dome and you will find the hotel right next door. So while everyone else is walking past with their suitcases you are already settled in, and sat at your table outside the hotel with a glass of Prosecco relaxing and reflecting on what a gem of a hotel you have found, because it is a gem. The staff are very accomodating, as soon as you walk through the door of this wonderful hotel it feels like home, the room we had was a triple, very well decorated with a stunning bathroom, soft towels, plenty of hot water and a hairdryer. The beds were a good size and the room had a fridge and a safe for no extra charge. Breakfast, although it was only a continental was adequate and a welcome start to the day in a pleasant environment, the staff again very friendly. I could not rate this hotel highly enough and it's a wonderful base for anyone visiting Venice.Some other information I would like to share if you are planning a trip to Venice and landing at Marco Polo Airport walk out to where the buses stop and take the Blue ATVO coach to Piazzale Roma only 3 euros, a cheap way to get to the above hotel and it only takes 20 mins. Also if you choose to stay at the above hotel and want to try a lovely restaurant walk down the alley way to the left of the hotel as you walk out of the front entrance and part way down on the left is a restaurant called Ostaria al Vecio Pozzo, the food is mouth watering and used alot by the locals, which is always a good sign.This hotel and the location of it made our trip to Venice as I am sure it would for anyone reading this review.

<Author>Billrover
<Content>Fantastic Hotel We stayed for 3 nights in the Antiche Figure and I have to say that it lived up to all the previous Trip Advisor reviews I'd read before going. All the staff were extremely friendly and helpful. The bedroom was a gem, overlooking the Grand Canal and was extremely well decorated and was spotlessly clean. The TV broke on day 1 and a brand new one was delivered within the hour. The breakfast room is small but the buffet breakfast is excellent. The hotel is easy to find near to the Railway station and The Piazzala Roma where the airport bus arrives. I would advise you to get the bus in from the airport - 3 Euros as you will have plenty of opportunities to use the Vaporettos (water buses) during your stay and a Water taxi will cost 80 Euros from the airport and take longer to get there.The best value and most interesting trip was the Secret Itineries Tour of the Doges Palace. Only 25 people on the tour and only in 3 languages so the English tour gets booked up with Americans, Dutch, Germans Scandinavians etc. You therefore must book in advance on the internet as the tour will be full on the day.Walking to the Rialto will take 15 mins from the hotel and St Marks will take 25mins and it is quite easy to get lost in the small alleyways. However if you follow the yellow signs its easy and its also easy getting back to the hotel as you just follow the Railway signs (Ferrovia) which are all over town.

<Author>sarahog
<Content>Antiche Figure, absolutely fantastic I visited the hotel Antiche Figure over the bank holiday weekend at the end of August with my mother, having done much research on Tripadvisor for the right place to stay. We couldn't have picked anywhere better.Rooms: The room we had was very large by european standards, it was a twin bedded room overlooking the Grand Canal. We had paid in advance for a grand canal room and definitely felt it was worth the extra 50 euros per night. In total, the room cost 180 euros per night and we were there for four nights.The beds were huge for single beds, very comfortable and fresh. They were made up everyday by the friendly maid. The room also had a TV and an internet socket. It was decorated in a traditional italian style with beautiful furnishings and exceptional attention to detail. The room also has a minibar, safe and large cupboards. The bathroom was equally as lovely and was again large by european standards, decorated all in marble with two sinks, a toilet and a bath with shower. The lights were all traditional Murano glass lights. Both the room and bathroom were cleaned to a very high standard every day.Even though the room was over looking the canal, once the windows are shut you hear nothing. We could not hear the amazing storm we had, let alone the rumble of waterbuses.Staff: were incredibly accommodating. Prior to the trip they answered all email correspondances very quickly and if you phone them they speak perfect english and are more than helpful. I also heard the staff speak very good spanish and french while we were there. When we arrived, we were supplied with a map of Venice and were pointed in the direction of the main sites. We were also given a free trip to Murano and tour around one of the glass factories, which was really lovely. It was very nice to be able to arrive by water taxi, which are otherwise horrendously expensive! We just went down one morning to inquire about the trip assuming we'd have to give notice but they booked it there and then and 15 minutes later we were in the taxi. The lady that served the breakfast in the morning was always so polite, happy and helpful, as were all the other staff. Breakfast itself was a small buffet, consisting of croissants, rolls, cheeses, meats, cereals, yoghurts, eggs, fruit, juices and hot drinks. A great way to start a long days sightseeing!Location: The hotel Antiche Figure is situated exactly opposite the railway station and about 5 minutes walk from Piazzale Roma (the last place that cars are allowed in the city). It was so convenient. From Marco Polo airport just take the ATVO bus costing 3 euros to Piazzale Roma (it takes about 20 minutes) and then head for the green domed church and scalzi bridge on the grand canal. You can also get a road taxi to piazzale roma but it will cost about 30 euros. Alternatively you can arrive by water taxi, but they are incredibly expensive, usually about 80 euros from the airport. If arriving from Treviso airport, you can get the ATVO bus from there for about 4.50 euros which arrives in the same place. Always remember to buy airport bus tickets from the office at the airport or, for the return journey, from the office in piazzale roma in advance. Although on the map the hotel looks like it is far from the main hub of Venice, this is simply not true. Venice is a small place and it only takes about 15-20 minutes to walk to the Rialto and St Marks area. It is a benefit to be far away from St Marks Square as you will find that the restaurants further out give much better value for money. If you can't face the walk, the waterbus stop is right outside the hotel across the bridge. You can buy a one day ticket for 10.50 euros or 3 day ticket for 22 euros. You can also buy a card called the VeniceCard blue/orange which give waterbus use and discounts at many museums and churches.If you head up to the Cannareggio region to the north there are some lovely restaurants. One restaurant which i WOULD NOT recommend is the Mirabar between the hotel and piazzale roma. It is poor value for money and the service is appauling too!Another nice thing about the hotel is that it has a small bar which is lovely at night. You can sit outside and watch the world go by.Although not to do with the hotel, I must recommend a particular tour at the Doge's Palace, called the 'Secret Itineries' tour. This needs ot be booked a few days in advance, and can be done so on the internet or by phone. The official price is 15 euros per adult, though some websites charge a lot more. We phoned up the palace 4 days before arrival but when we arrived they had lost the reservation number and claimed it was our fault and handed it back to us. It took about 25 minutes of 'discussions' to sort it out but eventually they let us go anyway even though they said it was all our fault and not their responsibility. Half way around the tour, the guide presented us with a reference number asking if it was ours, which it matched exactly, it had been lost in the office, no apology...The tour itself however is fantastic, it takes you to all the locked rooms in the doge's palace. You get to see the torture chambers, learn all about the system and hear Casanova's tale and see the cells where he was kept prisoner. I would also recommend a tour of the theatre La Fenice. It costs 7 euros each (6 euros on presentation of a waterbus ticket at the ACTV office in piazzale roma). it is very good value and they run tours in all different languages. So, the reason I have given the Antiche Figure 5/5 is because it is exceptional value for a 3* superior hotel. I doubt you would find another hotel at this price to match the Antiche Figure. Sorry to also include other information, but felt it might be useful!!! I would recommend the hotel's website for pictures of the rooms and location etc.

<Author>cami612
<Content>A Lovely Little Hotel in Venice My sister and I just returned from a long weekend in Venice, and were very pleased with the Hotel Antiche Figure. The rooms are not huge, but very clean and well-appointed. The staff are friendly, professional, and very helpful (special thanks to Gwendolina (sp?) and Alessandro). It is well worth booking a canal view room. We arrived before our room had been vacated (checkout is noon), and agreed to stay our first night in a non-canal view room, which was small, but we wanted to get out and about. The next day we were moved to room 412, which is one of the largest rooms, canal view, no balcony, non-smoking. The buffet breakfast, which is included in the price, is from 7 until 10, and includes croissants, rolls, yogurt, cheese, fruit, cereal, cold cuts, etc. The hotel is across the Grand Canal from the railway station, and a short walk from the bus station in Piazzale Roma, but our room was quiet nevertheless. If you arrive by train, walk over the Scalzi bridge -- the hotel is next to the church with the green dome. If you arrive by bus (take the blue ATVO express bus from Marco Polo airport, 3 euros) just walk down the Grand Canal toward the aforementioned church. We highly recommend Ristorante Ribo, which is a 5 minute walk from the hotel, in Fondamenta Minotto. It isn't cheap (dinner for two, with antipasto, pasta, main course, a bottle of wine and dessert costs about 140 euros) but well worth it-- we ate dinner there twice, and the seafood is delicious. We will certainly stay at Antiche Figure again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Hotel! We stayed in this lovely hotel for 4 nights in may 2005. The location was perfect for us as we arrived from Rome by train and just had to walk over the bridge to the hotel. This was great as we had 2 heavy bags with us. We got the bus to the airport when the holiday was over and the bus station is also very close. The staff were very friendly and helpful and gave us a great map with directions to all the sights. The room was much better than we expected it to be and was absolutely spotless. The breakfast was fine but it was difficult to get a table some mornings. But we were in no hurry anyway. We walked everywhere and found some restaurants that were great value - there were plenty of locals eating there too and the food was amazing. We never ate near Piazza san Marco as the food and wine is a rip off there - much better value in the small squares of Dorso Duro. I would recommend this hotel to all my friends and will definitely stay there again.

<Author>HDM
<Content>What a charming hotel! We've just returned from 3 days at the Antiche Figure and we loved it! It's absolutely charming and elegant and spotlessly clean. It's across from the train station which was perfect for us since we were coming into Venice by train from Florence and all we had to do was wheel our suitcases across the bridge and practically into the door of the hotel. It's true that you will have to ride a few stops longer on the vaporetto to get to some places but hey, it's not exactly a hardship riding down the Grand Canal of Venice. That said, if you like to walk, it's not difficult to walk to the Rialto area. We did it several times. I had originally booked a room on the city-side of the hotel because I was concerned about noise since my husband is a light sleeper but my younger (but wiser) sister insisted that it was a waste to book a Canal-front hotel and not get a Canal-front room. I had originally booked on expedia but since Venice was our last stop in Italy and we were only going to be there three nights, I threw caution to the winds and paid 45EUR extra per night for a deluxe room. And was I ever glad! Our room (room 201, I think) had a little balcony that looked out onto the Grand Canal, gondolas and vaporetti. The room was large with a king-sized bed, an extra single bed, lots of closet space and a beautiful Murano-glass chandelier. The bathroom was incredible -- all wood and marble with three matching glass chandelier sconces on the mirror and a large bath/shower. Noise was no problem at all. It's not a particularly noisy area, despite the busy streets, and the windows are double-glazed with heavy wooden shutters that can be closed as well.The lobby and lobby bar were charming (check out the painted ceiling beams in the lobby) as were the breakfast rooms. The breakfast buffet, although not the fullest we had on our trip, was certainly ample -- soft boiled eggs, baked goods, cheese, ham, cereal, juice fruit. My only complaint (and it's very minor) was that they had a machine that made coffee, cappuccino, espresso and hot chocolate and I would have prefered 'hand-made'. The Antiche Figure is plain on the outside but very charming and elegant on the inside. We loved it and wouldn't hesitate to stay there again.  
<Date>Jun 13, 2005

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A true value in in pricey Venice My wife and I stayed at the Antiche Figure for only two nights on April 12, 13, 2005. As with all of the hotels in our two week Italian tour, Tripadvisor was a factor in hotel selection. This hotel was THE nicest one we stayed in during our trip, and we selected hotels from the top of Tripadvisor's list in Rome, Sorrento, and Florence in the $250/nt price range.The hotel is very well located to all forms of transportation, the train station and vaporetto stop right across the canal, and the bus/ land taxi station only a couple of blocks away in the Piazzale Roma. Getting to your hotel in Venice can be a real pain, but the Antiche Figure is ridiculously easy to get to no matter how you arrive in Venice. There is loads of shopping and eating three minutes walk away. We had reserved a Canal view balcony room several weeks prior and reconfirmed via e-mail two weeks before our stay. No Problem! The room far exceeded our expectations, it was lavishly appointed in true Venetian style, spotlessly clean and all of the amenities were in perfect working order. One could spend nearly twice as much for the same room closer to the Rialto bridge or San Marco, but there is no reason to do so if you can book this Hotel! It offers the true Venice experience with the added benefit of fronting on one of the widest and longest canal-side promenades in the city (Great people watching).We preferred to hear to the sounds of Venice at night by leaving the balcony door open, but if noise bothers you (which is not that much to begin with), everything is double-paned and you can close the door/window and shut out the noise.The staff is very helpful and make every effort to make sure your needs are met. Thank You, Hotel Antiche Figure for making our too short stay in Venice so fabulous!!

<Author>PeteWM
<Content>Style and quality...! My wife and I stayed here for 6 nights at the end of March. We booked direct and very much on the strength of other TripAdvisor reports. We were not disappointed. There were no problems with not getting the room we'd asked for - though I did send an email about a week before our trip to make sure that everything was o/k. On our arrival, Alessandro on reception was very welcoming and ready with informative and helpful advice, and this set the scene for the rest of our stay - the hotel staff were always friendly and very efficient. The location is excellent; only about 5 minutes away from either the bus or train stations, so no need to trundle your luggage over bridges for miles before you reach the hotel! Yet for all that, it still has a very strong feel of Venice by virtue of its position right on the Grand Canal, with its view of the Scalzi bridge. And after a day's exploring, it was great to sit at the pavement tables outside the hotel, with an ice cream and coffee and just watch the world go by!Our room was typically Venetian in style, with a little balcony overlooking the Grand Canal. Very romantic, but, if you're a light sleeper, be aware that there can be some noise from canal traffic (the vaporetta stop is opposite the hotel, and there's a gondala jetty just outside). Take a tip, close the outside window shutters and this may help to bring the sound down to a manageable level.Breakfast was included. This was a cold buffet breakfast, but we thought it was more than adequate - a very good selection, very well presented, and as much coffee as you want - and the breakfast room was bright and extremely clean and very distinctively furnished.Eating out in Venice can be a bit of a lottery. It can be very expensive for food which is nothing special (and I don't mean pizza or pasta, etc) and for service which can be frankly indifferent, and fresh vegetables seem to be a scarcity on most menus. Shop around and find what suits you and your pocket. We found an excellent place 15 minutes stroll away; the Alla Palazzina on Ponte delle Guglie (good food and at the end of the meal you weren't hassled for tips!); or for lunch, and if you're down in the Arsenale area, the osteria da Amelia e Sergio (not a lot of English spoken, but you can soon make yourself understood. The bill came to euros and cents! A novelty, and they very kindly said Oh, just pay us the euros!We loved Venice, what a fascinating city. And when we next visit, we'll make sure we stay at this hotel again. As travellers, we have high standards and high expectations, but we would fully recommend this hotel without any hesitation.Enjoy it, and enjoy Venice.  
<Date>Apr 11, 2005

<Content>Problems with Reservation (again!) As with another reviewer who contributed on September 14, 2004, I had a confirmed reservation at the hotel with a Grand Canal View. I had booked this at a special Expedia rate a month prior to my arrival and had confirmation of the booking. However upon arrival (I arrived at 6 pm) I was told that there had been a problem with my reservation and they had booked me into another hotel five minutes away. As it happens, this was also on Piazze Roma and instead of a view of the Grand Canal, I was afforded views of the main bus station out front and a car park out back. I too was upgraded to a 'Suite', although in any 4* hotel in the USA this would have qualified as a normal room in terms of its size. Although this was perfectly acceptable to me as I was there on business (the room at the 'new' hotel was clean and recently renovated, and the hotel staff were very friendly and helpful) I have to admit I would have been furious had I been there on a romantic weekend.I have raised this issue with Expedia and asked them to investigate. However, in the meantime, if you really want to stay at this hotel and have a room with a view, I too would encourage people to also receive confirmation (preferably in writing) directly from the hotel that the hotel have not only received the reservation (which undoubtedly they will have), but that the hotel will honour it and not move the guest to another hotel.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>First visit to Venice For our first ever visit to Venice, my partner and I booked 4 nights at the Antiche Figure for 4 nights in February 2005 through Expedia.THe hotel is conveniently situated for all forms of transport.Both the Railway and Bus Stations are within a 5 minute walk. The No5 bus brings you direct from Marco Polo Airport. They run at least evey 30 minutes during the day and the fare is 2 Euros.Across the canal from the hotel is the Vaperetto Public Water Bus Stop at Ferrovia, right outside the rail station. Catch the No1 Vaperetto to travel down the Grand Canal towards the Rialto Bridge and St Marks Square. A 3 day pass costs 22 Euros, a really good buy.We both thought the hotel was fantastic. Recently refurbished to a very high standard both the rooms we had were of a good size, spotlessly clean and nicely furnished.We stayed for 2 nights on the fourth floor at the side of the hotel. This was perfectly fine but we enquired about the availability of a room overlooking the canal. Subject to availability this can be arranged for a supplement of 25 to 50 Euros per night.(Per room not person).The view that this room gave down the canal was fantastic. I would recommend paying the supplement for at least part of your stay if not all.Like most visitors we were bowled over by Venice and delighted to have stayed in such a nice hotel. We would recommend it to anybody.

<Author>Travelguru4u
<Content>Bellisimo!-BRAVO! This hotel was in a GREAT location!!! The room was VERY clean and comfortable. The bathroom was SPOTLESS and the shower had excellent water pressure. The staff was extremely helpful and pleasant. The breakfast was sufficent. This hotel was FANTASTIC!!!! Helpful hints:From Marco Polo Airport take the BLUE BUS to Piazzeli Roma. Be sure to have Euro's in change to buy your ticket-3 Euro's per person.Behind the Piazzeli Roma ticket booth is a walkway along the Grand Canal-make a right, go over two small bridges and you are there-on your right. It is directly across the Grand Canal from the Santa Lucia Train Station. This area, Santa Croce, is in walking distance of the Rialto and San Marco area. If you don't want to walk, take the vaperatto-SP? #1-this stops frequently along the Grand Canal or #82 which makes fewer stops along the Grand Canal. ***You can buy a 72 hour ticket for 22 Euros/per person at the Piazzeli Roma ticket booth.****To the right of the Santa Lucia Train Station there are plenty of shops and restaurants.Try to walk. You will get to see more of the canals and homes. You can't get lost!! There are destination signs throughout the city. When wanting to return to Marco Polo Airport buy a bus ticket at the Piazelli Roma ticket booth. It will cost 2 Euro's per person. You will need to board the YELLOW BUS #5-Aeroporto.This is a beautiful city-ENJOY!!!!!!

<Author>longrider
<Content>Great Hotel Stayed at the hotel in October 2004. Location is opposite from train station over a bridge. All bridges have stairs (no ramp) and you must drag your luggage up/down. The front desk was very nice. Breakfast was good. Had originally booked a room in the hotel, but arrived early and got a room in the apartment. We got it for the same price, very quiet and very roomy (2 bedrooms, washing machine, iron, refrig, stove, kitchen). The apartment is in the same building. Never got to see what the hotel rooms were like, so no comment. It was nice to have a big place after staying in a few other places in Italy and having small places. I guess the key is to not look like a target. Booked hotel through hotels ($140e night). If you think you are going to have to change your schedule, it is easier to find your best price online and then call the hotel directly (011-39-041-2759486) and book it. This gives you flexibility with the hotel to extend/decrease your stay without hotels.com policy.

<Author>DotStaffs
<Content>Excellent in every way The location of the hotel is excellent. Take a bus from the Airport to Piazzale Roma, cross the bridge and you are there. The first impression was very good of a clean hotel. It was slightly spoiled by reception asking us if we would like to upgrade to a canal view room at a discounted rate (we had a side view). After a long journey we didn't want to feel a sales pressure. However there was no pressure and we stayed in our original room. It was smallish but very adequate, nicely furnished with a very nice bathroom. We had a good view of the Grande Canal.Transport is very easy. You are very close to the train station, vaparetto and just a 10 minute walk from the bus station.We stayed for 4 nights, September 2004. The breakfasts were excellent, cereals, yogurts, fruit, meats, cheese, croissants etc. Staff were helpful and friendly. We would certainly go back to this hotel.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Buyer beware.... I had confirmed reservations at this hotel through Expedia. I chose it based upon reviews on this site and proximity to the train station. I was also hoping for a room overlooking the Grand Canal. Upon showing up, the hostess informed me they had problems confirming my room. I wasn't sure what she meant as she has my reservation but somehow they didn't have a room for me. I couldn't explore further due to Italian/English Communication barrier. Needless to stay they provided a room at another hotel (with an upgrade room to a junior suite to sweeten the blow). The hotel was about 5-10 walk away and was conveniently next to the Venice bus station off the beaten path. I'm curious about the mixup, and I guess I'll never find out, but my recommendation is to confirm you actually will be staying at this hotel before your trip.
